when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她的確做過一些 , 但真正的事情是說未來會比這個還要多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙來了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 在1936年 , 再次發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是從數學的角度來的 , 但圖靈告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不管你怎麼製作電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你的電腦的機械 , 像是babbage的 , 或是電子的 , 像是現在的電腦 , 或者是未來的細胞 , 或者 , 再一次 , 再一次 , 再一次 , 再次進入奈米技術 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 。 所有的東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種程度上 , 計算本質上是有的 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂追求論點 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你會看到這個連結 , 你說babbage是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它有能力用電腦來做我們現今所做的事 , 只有很緩慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓各位了解 , 它的記憶有多慢 , 大約有1k 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用打孔卡 , 被送進去 , 跑的速度大約是zx81的一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一包拉姆 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加上很多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天那帶給我們哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫的這個分析引擎所寫 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一組是一組我們稱之為計劃28的計劃 , 這也是我從doronswaade開始的慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的計算機 , 也是開這個計劃來建立差異引擎的那個人 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部這裡 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案計畫有幾個部分要把它
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其一是babbage的檔案掃描
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	已經完成了 。 第二個是關於這些計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是那台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是要在科學博物館建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為 , 與其在你面前有小小的晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體操作 , 我看到cpu操作 , 我聽到它操作 。 我可能聞到它 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們將進行模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫道 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造過 , 因為他總是帶著新的計畫 , 但當它確實被建立起來 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我稍微為各位介紹一下它在動作中看起來是什麼樣子的 , 影片中只顯示了cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 還會加上 。 這是在行動中的添加機制 , 所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們會有
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個圖像填充的演講中 , 雅南•亞瑟伯特蘭展現了他近期對人類的三個項目 , 以及我們居住地的空拍攝 , 在他的系列《上方地球》中 , 來自全球各地的個人訪談 , 他的網路專案《六十億人》 , 他的《家》 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅南•亞瑟伯特納在廣角的地球上捕捉到脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以靠飛機來這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來到這裡來談生態學 , 一年內我排放的二氧化碳量和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼做呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我回家時必須殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來處理碳排放 , 就像我每次都一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我將展示一些我去年拍過的最後一張照片的例子 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省沙油 , 大量污染
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 ; 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省人們工作非op , 24小時到7小時 , 盡可能地萃取出石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們對石油盡頭的了解
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是一個長期的解決方案
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油比我們發現的還要多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的
coral reef in new caledonia .	新卡里多尼亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年之前被消滅 , 因為全球暖化 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	而且你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 。 我去年夏天拍過這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	十五年前不可能完成這張照片 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在在大西洋和太平洋之間開放了一種新的方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	北極的厚度從1960年起降低了40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	基里曼jaro的新面孔沒有冰 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	牠失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家的說法 , 在100年內 , 所有的山脈冰河都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像艾爾•高爾告訴過你 , 二十億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。
return of fish men .	回報魚的男人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	人類的五分之一仰賴魚類生活 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現在有70%的魚股被過度利用 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao , 如果我們不改變我們在2050年捕魚的系統 , 主要的海資源將在2050年消失 。

here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國這裡 , 百分之九十的玉米被用來餵食動物或做石油 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:這個地球已經有四十五億年了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 數億歲 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	而我們人類已經直立行走了2萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們已經成功地適應了 , 並且已經征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 不像其他數百萬的物種生活在我們旁邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我密切關注地球和它在天空高處的威爾人 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活和地球的幸福息息相關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、養殖 , 仍然是世界上的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	而把我們結合在一起的 , 遠大於分裂我們的東西 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都與地球的天賦有相同的需求 , 希望在我們自己之上升 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們還是繼續築牆 , 來讓我們分開 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天 , 我們最偉大的戰役是要保護我們星球的自然提供 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們已經徹底改變了人類的歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源在運作的低點
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集耕地正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不永續 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只試圖改善我們的生活
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們正以比地球更快的速度前進 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有改變這個趨勢的力量 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克展示了 「 便宜且快速的基因序列 」 即將要把健康照護調低 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生技、健康照護、科學、科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	richardresnick:歡迎來到基因革命
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示了人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩份大x染色體的複製品 ; 男人有x , 當然 , 還有y的那一小份複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩 , 但這只是小事讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 你會看到 , 當然 , 這是雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼是用這四個生化字母拼出來的 , 或者我們稱之為鹼基 , 對了:a、c、g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以丟出大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我在1280年的畫素上放一個鹼基 , 到800個解析度螢幕 , 我們需要300個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便說一下 , y染色體決定他們會想要排序它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年 , 實際上 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組被定序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本出版了 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	全都在機器上完成 , 看起來像這樣 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個鹼基的成本是非常緩慢的一美元 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以 , 現在我們所做的是 , 我們拿一個基因組 , 做成50份複本 , 我們把這些複本都切成50個鹼基的讀寫 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們將它帶入軟體中 , 重新組合起來 , 告訴你們這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 為了讓大家看一下這是什麼樣子 , 人類基因組計畫:3gabas , 對吧 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台在其中一台機器上運行:一週內有200gabas
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	而那200位將會改變到今年夏天600位 , 沒有這個步調緩慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以一個鹼基的價格 , 來排序一個鹼基 , 已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這等於在座各位在1998年用汽油填滿汽車 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星和後面兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc位置 , 所有醫療文獻的檔案庫 , 摩爾定律 , 舊的定序方式 , 以下是所有的新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個木號尺度 ; 你通常不會看到像那樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界對人類基因組的排序能力 , 大約是今年五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	而我們知道這個基於被安置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期的兩倍、三倍 , 或可能是四倍 , 年復一年 , 對可見的未來而言 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室特別代表所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因學研究所
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對贏得這場競賽 , 順便說一下 , 新月球 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學意味著什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她帶著第2階段的雌激素接受乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她回來時帶著三次c卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時回來 , 卵巢癌有更多 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著敏銳的失血症回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後死去 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	所以 , 首先 , 這個女人接受治療的方式 , 在十年內 , 看起來會像血流一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為像我同事rickwilson這樣的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 她決定去看這位女子後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	然後他定序 , 取出皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 以及癌症的骨髓 , 他在幾週內將它們兩個基因組定序 , 沒有什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他在軟體中比較了這兩組基因組 , 他發現 , 在其它東西中 , 是一組刪減 , 一個在tp53的特定基因中 , 兩千個巴西的刪減 ,
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這個敏銳的突變 , 你有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這並不能幫助這位女士 , 但它確實有嚴重的意義 , 深刻的影響著她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果它們有相同的突變 , 就會得到這種基因測試 , 並且了解它 , 那麼它們可以去取得普通的螢幕 , 並且能早期追上癌症 , 並且能夠顯著更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我介紹一下現在的啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺症 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是一位非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信這些症狀不符合 , 透過一些英雄性的努力和很多網路搜尋 , 她得以說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的 , 是對應的dystonia
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了woropa , 他們的症狀確實有改善 , 但他們並沒有完全不一樣的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	原來這張照片裡的先生是一位叫喬•貝瑞的傢伙 , 他很幸運能成為一家名為生命科技公司的順序 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家公司之一 , 讓這些大量的完整基因定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子做完排序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 一連串基因突變 , 叫做spr , 負責生產血清素 , 在其他東西當中 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在wolopa的頂端 , 他們給了這些孩子一種血清素的前兆藥物 , 他們現在就很正常了 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 若沒有完整的基因序列 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	而在幾年前 , 這花費是十萬美元 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在百元之後的一年 , 給予或花一年
that's how fast this is moving .	這移動的速度有多快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡是小尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和烏賊槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 帶著這種不滿的肚子 , 像饑荒受害者一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西時 , 他的腸子基本上會打開來 , 把糞便噴到他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以 , 一百多次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽 , 說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 。 我在這麼多的痛苦中 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子的基因組定序 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 一個基因突變 , 負責控制細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以理論上 , 他對食物的產生有一些免疫反應 , 基本上 , 這是自然反應 , 造成一些編程細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但調節它的基因是壞的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也說明了骨髓移植的治療方式 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的哀傷復原後 , 他現在用1口醬吃牛排 。

today , it's here .	今天 , 在這裡

which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你想到地球上人類的足跡 , 以及我們能維持食物生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植新的玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 和其他作物是高容忍性的乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就必須繼續成長 , 繼續吃基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天唯一會採取的立場 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫•克拉夫•戴莫斯 , 他的骨髓採集了新裝置 , 很快就收集了救命的骨髓 , 用最小的痛苦給捐贈者 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中發現的成人幹細胞 , 可以用來治療許多臨終狀況 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是小兒科癌症醫生 , 史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床專注一直是骨髓移植手術 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年 , jillboltetaylor的靈感並不是人腦 , 但我的確帶來了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 大多數有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 例如白血病和淋巴瘤 , 以及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛大學做移植研究 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 拯救白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 實際上 , 我們要如何收集這個骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	嗯 , 我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 麻醉師 , 護士 , 還有另一位來自我的醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃在桌上 , 我們用這種小針 , 你知道的 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法基本上就是把這個通過軟組織 , 然後把它打進硬骨頭 , 進入tuchus──那是一個技術名詞──每次用針筒來刺穿大約10磅的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠交給護士 。 她把牠刮成一根小塊 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到了這張手臂的尾聲 , 我手上有叫聲 , 更不用說鮑勃 , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 像是瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道嗎 , 這個程序在大約40年沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了一個極少侵入性的方法 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓採礦者 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓採礦者 , 它的運作方式就是在這裡所展示的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的看診病人
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只是進入髖部的前面或臀部的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有個彈性、有力的導管 , 帶著特殊的電線接管 , 會留在骨髓裡 , 遵循臀部的輪廓 , 隨著臀部移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它會讓你非常迅速地有抱負 , 或吸出豐富的骨髓很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以做到多次通過那相同的入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃可以拿到一根刺、當地的麻醉劑 , 把這個收割當成一種病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛拿到一點小格子 。
and played around with this a little bit .	玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩種大型動物 , 豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令我們驚訝的是 , 我們不只得到骨髓 , 還得到骨髓採取的幹細胞活動的十倍 , 相較於正常的設備 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才剛核准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是現場的病人 。 你可以看到它遵循了靈活的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人身上 , 將有兩個通過 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地的麻醉劑下進行的 , 作為一個病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們又得到了大約三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比同一個病人所做的標準方法還要多 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	那你為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是一個非常豐富的成人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成年的幹細胞在我們的身體裡 , 包括我們骨髓裡的血液幹細胞 , 我們已經用它作為幹細胞療法的形式 , 超過40年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年中 , 已經有一爆炸用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人的其他疾病 , 例如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經學上治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出來 , 正在商業化 , 今年 , 第二代的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能得到更多的幹細胞 , 翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人去簽署成為潛在救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能讓你可以把自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年紀越來越小 , 更健康時 , 未來就應該要用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這裡有一張我們骨髓移植倖存者的照片 , 他們每年在史丹佛聚集一堂聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這樣的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garrettlisi所呈現的宇宙有爭議性的新模型 , 可能只能回答所有大問題 。 如果什麼都沒有 , 它是最美麗的8維模型 , 基本粒子和力你所見過的 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	gaarretttlisi在他的理論上所說的一切
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我會盡我所能地描述粒子物理學的美好 , 沒有方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	原來我們可以從珊瑚中學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭部都包含了上千個個別的聚合物 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚合物是持續在繁殖和分支 , 成為基因上一模一樣的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個超級智慧的珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他到底是如何在這個特定的地點與鄰居相比 , 如果只是偶然 , 還是命運 , 還是什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們打算把溫度調高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題是完全愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以相當的表示 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的疤痕來證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚合物會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居顯然是一模一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在所有其他的地點也一樣 , 但他們卻是獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支為不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	與我們不同的是 , 超級智慧的珊瑚會獨有準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們我們的現實是持續分支成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗到一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異性最初是由erwin薛丁格和他的貓描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , 薛丁格在一個有放射性樣本的盒子裡 , 由量子力學定律 , 分支成一個它被放射的狀態 , 一個它沒有的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本放射線輻射的樹枝中 , 它會產生一種觸發物 , 釋放出中毒和薛丁格已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真實都被各個個個體獨立的體驗
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	相對來說 , 另一種也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人都只會經歷個人的存在 , 我們也不會看到其他的樹枝 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	彷彿我們每一個人 , 如薛丁格這裡 , 都是珊瑚分支成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 世界是如何以微小的尺度運作的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用單一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都可以 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是要描述什麼可以發生 , 什麼也不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都朝下到幾何學以及小粒子的交互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	而事情只能發生在這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我會先描述一下我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是什麼 , 以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 一束質子和反質子的束縛會加速接近光速 , 並在撞擊中聚集 , 產生出一股純能量爆炸 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴射 , 上面有探測器和電腦 , 用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的cern的大型強子對撞機有17英哩的情況 , 當它運作時 , 畫出和蒙特利市一樣多的五倍力量 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法明確預測哪些粒子會在任何個體碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都實現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理的確告訴我們哪些粒子可以被產生 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量必須跟質子和反質子一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子的質量都比這個能量極限還大 , 對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新的粒子加速器是如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將推動這個能量限制了七倍以上之前做過的事所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在討論我們可能看到的東西之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整片亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大多數人都熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座很多人都做得不錯的活著把他們推過來 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中立的夥伴 , 叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷和非常微小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 上下的夸克有很大的質量 , 三分之三的組合來製造原子內的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些粒子在左手和右手的品種中出現 , 同時有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 它的載荷和第一代一樣 , 但有更高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子全都和各種力量粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力與電荷相互作用 , 通過稱為光子的粒子 ,
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力量 , 叫做 「 不可思議 」 , 「 弱力 」 , 只能與左撇子的物質互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶有不同種類的載荷 , 稱為顏色載荷 , 再來是三種不同的品種:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann--他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力的力量 , 能透過質量和旋轉 , 與物質相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	要了解這裡最重要的一點是 , 每一種力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量相互作用 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的對應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 給所有其他粒子帶來質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到這顆希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的奧秘是我們可能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要給你們看一段美麗的可能性 , 朝這場演說結束前看 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用它們的各種旋轉和載荷來算所有不同的粒子 , 就會有226顆 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	大量的粒子可以持續追蹤
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	似乎很奇怪大自然會擁有這麼多的基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的收費來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 一個負荷 , 夸克則有電荷三分之一 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合起來製造質子時 , 它有一個總電荷加1 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 它有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是其他兩個電荷的組合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷的電荷散佈在這個二度載荷空間中 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力根據超荷和弱荷的作用力與物質相互作用 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 統一的心電圖 」 模型 , 它被放回1967年 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部分人都只熟悉電荷而不是這兩種原因是因為希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊這裡的希格斯 , 有一個很大的質量 , 打破了這個心電圖案的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	讓弱力變得非常微弱 , 藉由給弱粒子一個大的質量 , 讓弱力變得非常微弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	自從這個巨大的希格斯坐落在這個圖表的水平方向後 , 電磁學的光子會持續不動 , 沿著這個載荷空間的垂直方向與電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	因此 , 電磁力和弱力被這種在二維空間中載荷的粒子的模式所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力的力量傳出它的兩個載荷方向 , 並沿這些方向描繪出波力粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維載荷空間中被描繪出來 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用時 , 大自然都會保持完美的平衡 , 沿著這四個載荷方向進行 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和一個反粒子碰撞 , 它會產生一股能量 , 總載荷的四個載荷方向是0 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來只要它擁有相同的能量維持一個總載量為零
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子 , 可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須永遠平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可以腐化成電子和一個反中子 , 這三個仍然加到零充電 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的圖案並不只是很漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們哪些互動是可以發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 以獲得更好的觀察力相互作用 , 這有很好的六角形對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 強力粒子 , 例如這一個 , 和有色的夸克互動 , 例如這個綠色的 , 用不同的顏色充電 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強交互作用每秒發生數百萬次在我們身體的每一個原子裡 , 將原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應三種力量並不是故事的結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再納入兩個載荷對應地心引力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	包括這些時 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都會分開 , 在六度載荷空間中給出一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它是相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這種模式符合我們目前最佳的知識 , 了解大自然是如何以這些小粒子的微小尺度建造的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們肯定知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	這些粒子的極限在實驗中 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道這些小尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙與這些小尺度合作的方式非常美麗 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的和舊的想法關於我們還不知道的事情 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們希望獨自使用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把手伸到整個enchilada上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找到所有的粒子和力來構成我們宇宙的完整圖像 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 我們會發現 , 當實驗達到更高的能量時 ,
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以在粒子物理學中有個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不太對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的圖案中浮現出來 , 與希格斯粒子如何打破電波圖案來賦予電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新的電荷方向的新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子沿著這個方向的載荷 , 然後我們就可以把粒子轉向他人 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以用六個載荷維度來建構標準載荷作為七個載荷維度的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特別的選擇對應於1973年pati和salam的大統一理論
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些粒子似乎缺少的缺口 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	一名物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包括建立的圖案是次級的 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們可以預測從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩個新力粒子的存在 , 它應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 考慮一個關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:第二代和第三代物質擁有和第一代相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是獨一無二的被它們的六個載荷所辨識出來的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間中 , 它們彼此坐在上面 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那我們就可以把獨一無二的載荷分配給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個模式看起來是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質的關係 , 由一個叫做 「 審判性 」 的對稱 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這八度載荷的特定模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構的一部分 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大例外的謊言團體的模式 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言小組是平滑、彎曲的形狀 , 有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這個圖案中的每一個點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙如何以最小的尺度運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀在八度載荷空間中生活的模式是精確的美麗的它總結了數千個這些基本粒子之間的可能相互作用每一個都只是這複雜的形狀的表面
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	隨著我們旋轉 , 我們可以看到其中許多複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	藉由一個特定的旋轉 , 我們可以在八度空間中觀察這個模式 , 沿著一個對稱軸 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 就像任何統一物體一樣 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 那裡有新的粒子被這個圖案所要求 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個缺口 , 其中兩個已經被帕塔納姆粒子填滿了 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從他們在這個模式的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的稀有場地 , 但有顏色充電和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子完成了這個圖案 , 給我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有很深的數學根 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的前景:這個偉大的數學美麗物可以用最小的尺度來描述粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	這種認為大自然被數學所描述的概念完全不是新穎的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫了這個: 「 大自然的大書 , 它不斷地對我們的凝視開放 , 以數學的語言寫出來 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 , 若沒有人性無法理解單一字詞 ; 若沒有這些 , 就會在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊蕩 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我也試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 用三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形來描述粒子物理學的數學 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這個東西時 , 數學可以組成一個暗色迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 很放心的是 , 在這數學的核心是純、美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這數學將我們的宇宙描述成一個不斷增長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個可能的位置互動 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式出現 , 使用大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們或許可以看出大自然是否使用這種e8圖案 , 或不同的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程 , 是要參與的美好冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合這個e8圖案的粒子 , 那會非常非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對這個e8理論卻不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 蠻糟的 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是非常冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其它類似的 , 都是長時間拍的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力工作 , 知道這些想法大部分都可能不會成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理學就是這樣:有許多的狂熱 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有任何大型投資 , 就會很難在不成功時放棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有東西沒用 , 你就得把它丟出去 , 試試別的東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 要維持聖經並在這種不確定性中達到快樂的唯一方法就是維持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我曾盡我所能的過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的人生 , 在物理學、愛和衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向之間 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	如此一來 , 即使我工作的物理學一無所有 , 我仍然知道我過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去10年來 , 我住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在是宇宙中最偉大的奧秘之一 , 對我父母來說 , 我是如何能一直存活下來 , 不需要全職就業 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我會讓你們深入這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在maui的家裡辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你們可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的觀點都很相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇過非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心租金讓我花時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	生活在遊牧時的存在已經很艱苦 , 但它讓我可以生活在美麗的地方 , 在我的生活中保持平衡 , 我一直很高興 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超智慧珊瑚掛在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以 , 我很高興受邀來ted演講 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概了解了百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我會聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你所有事物的理論都看得出來:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 至少少數人感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你對的話 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說我們應該要想到宇宙 , 在它的心臟裡 , 最小的東西 , 是不是一個可能性的e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度 , 還是... ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	高爾:嗯 , 現在我給你們看的圖案與我們所知的小粒子物理學對應到一個非常美麗的形狀
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說的 , 我們一定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	那個形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 和它符合這個e8圖案的方式可能是其餘的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我為你們展示的這些點圖案 , 其實代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 會在我們所經歷的時空中扭曲、移動和跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們看到的所有這些小粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但弦理論學家 , 正如我所理解的 , 用更小的弦來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面振動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們應該如何看待一個與e8相連的電子呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	高爾:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 隨著形狀在時空中移動 , 它在扭曲 。 當它移動時 , 會轉動的方向 , 會是我們看到的粒子 。 克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子相連的形狀如何 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	更大嗎 ? 更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	高爾:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子就是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論上被解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性都在同時擴大和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是為什麼我用類比來珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	用這種方式 , e8的進展方式是 , 在時空的每一刻 , 都被附著的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的 , 形狀扭曲了方向 , 隨著形狀在彎曲的表面移動時 , 扭曲的形狀是基本粒子的樣子 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 他們把自己呈現為點 , 並用這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能讓這一切更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:其實不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	喚起一種奇蹟的感覺 , 我當然也想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	謝謝大家 。 這絕對是非常吸引人的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍•古德爾談到tacare和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助非洲鎮民在受威脅的動物旁邊生活 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古德拉協助人類和動物一起生活在一起 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 賈莫 , 古丁abend , 邦索爾 , 但我們也可以──噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所作的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從一群巢穴傳到下一個 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想要拿起我的演講 , 來自昨天zeray離開的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個令人驚嘆、三歲的澳洲小孩塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過有關人類的歷史、家譜 , 透過dna基因檔案的人類 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	那是一位古生物學家 , 已故路易斯.李克 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的路徑 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	那時是非常不尋常的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點普遍 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺跡 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以很清楚地知道那些從化石中看起來是什麼樣子 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 和他們從不同工藝品中發現的一些東西 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為呢 ? 那是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張而且現在是一個相當普遍的理論如果我們發現行為模式在我們最接近的活生生生的親戚身上 , 大猩猩 , 和人類今天 , 也許那些行為存在於類似的物種中 , 人類的祖先大約七百萬年前 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從古老、古老的過去帶給我們這些特徵 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你今天在課本上看處理人類演化的教科書 , 你經常發現人們推測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比其他生物更像我們 , 我們在ted大會上也聽過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 它仍然讓我對黑猩猩的行為作出評論 , 在某些方面 , 牠們的行為是如此的像我們 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有他或她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給了他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年以上 , 雖然我們認為他們大部分的人可能不會在野外變成60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲爾先生 。 女生在她十一或十二歲時 , 生下了她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五六年就有一個寶寶 , 長期依賴童年 , 當孩子在護理時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 然後騎在她背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 童年對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 就像是對我們來說 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同的動物演化過程中變得更複雜 , 所以我們發現 , 學習在個人的生命史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	而年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察他們的長輩們所做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 正是這種方式 , 不同工具的行為現在已經在非洲各個不同的黑猩猩族群中看到了 , 這些人是如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 這樣我們就能把這些工具的行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語的語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 許多都很相似 , 甚至是一模一樣的 , 在同樣的情境下形成 。 希臘黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、握手、在後面拍打 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	並且揮之不去 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多很多同情心的例子 , 前驅者去愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們就像我們一樣 , 對他們的天性有著暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極度殘暴 , 甚至是種原始戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常具侵略性的行為 , 大部分的情況 , 都是針對鄰近社會團體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們非常有侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩們 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物都更能幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物王國之間沒有一條尖銳的線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線條 , 隨時都在做更多觀察時 , 越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我1960年開始的研究 , 仍持續到今日 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外的複雜的社會生活中 , 比任何其他東西都更能幫助我們意識到我們是其中的一部分 , 而非與我們共享地球的驚人動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 發現黑猩猩 , 就像世界各地許多其他生物一樣 , 牠們的棲息地都在喪失 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它顯示了gombe的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	就在我飛越整個地區時 , 大約十六年前 , 意識到 , 在公園外面 , 這片森林 , 在1960年時 , 沿著塔尼卡湖東岸幾乎沒有破裂 , 那個地方很小 , 30平方公園 , 一個問題來到我腦海 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們怎麼可能甚至可以試著拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人在掙扎求生存時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比土地還多的人可以支援 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量增加了 , 來自緬甸和來自剛果湖的數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人 , 他們負擔不起從別處買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	改善人們生活在公園附近的村莊裡
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始 。 現在是24個 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探討 , 但包括樹木護士 , 最適合耕作的方法 , 目前非常惡劣 , 幾乎像沙漠般地落在這些山中 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤侵蝕的方式
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重獲過度使用的農地的方式 , 這樣在兩年內 , 就能再次生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民從井裡取得新鮮水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些學校教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與小群體的女性合作 , 提供她們的機會是微型貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們有 , 如同全世界的案例 , 大約95%的貸款都回報了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權女性 , 與教育合作 , 為女孩提供獎學金 , 讓他們能完成次等學校 , 清楚地了解 , 在世界各地 , 隨著女性教育的改善 , 家庭規模下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供有關家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫的結果 , 有些事正在發生 ,
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的情況是 , 居住在這24個村落的農夫們 , 而不是以一群白人來研究一大群猴子 , 順便說一下 , 很多店員現在都是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始了tacare計畫時 , 是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是坦尚尼亞的團隊 , 和村民談話 , 問他們對什麼感興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康感興趣 ; 他們對教育感興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間的發展 , 隨著他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白 , 隨著山丘的上層層被樹木砍伐 , 所以你有這種可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土滑落 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們稱之為更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在全國公園外面的區域 , 延伸到非常惡劣的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活水準時 , 他們其實同意把百分之十到二十的土地放在高地邊 , 所以再一次 , 隨著樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩就會有葉子走廊 , 讓牠們可以和國家公園外的其他遺傳性族群互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功的
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地區複製它 , 在其它的荒野地區 , 面臨極端族群壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們在討論ted的前幾天 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮有很大的一部分 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量居住在土地上的人不是那麼肥沃 , 特別是當你砍伐樹木時 , 你就把土壤打開 , 當絕望的族群砍掉越來越多的樹木 , 這樣他們就可以嘗試為自己和家人種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 有什麼事必須給予 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他的問題不僅是非洲 , 其他的發展中國家 , 的確 , 到處都是我們對地球所做的事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家e.o.wilson說如果地球上每一個人都維持了平均歐洲或美國人的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 。 但是我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 在這裡 , 我們可說是最有智慧的人 , 曾走過地球 , 帶著這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠被這些ted會議所描繪出來的科技 , 然而我們卻在摧毀我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在做了重大決定之前 , 曾經坐下來問自己: 「 這個決定如何影響我們七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定 , 我不是特別在這裡談到非洲 , 而是已開發國家重大決策 , 涉及數百萬美元 , 而數百萬人 , 通常是基於: 「 這會如何影響到下一個股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行 , 談論黑猩猩和牠們消失的森林所面臨的問題時 , 我了解到越來越多的非洲問題 , 可能是前一次殖民地開發的大門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲談話 , 在美國談話 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些糟糕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們知道我在說的那種 。 我說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣常常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水源可能是我們這個世紀所面臨的最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都是水被農業、工業和家庭化的化學物質所污染 , 這些化學物質仍然在世界各地被噴灑 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 像海嘯的效應越來越嚴重 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們還有其他溫室氣體燃燒的石化燃料 , 稱為 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候有一些問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是那些受影響較差的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	已經被影響的非洲
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱的情況更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當下雨的確到來時 , 它通常會導致洪水和苦難 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住在土地無法支撐的地區的人數太貧窮無法購買食物 , 無法遠離因為整片土地被降解 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會看到沙漠化的腐爛 , 令人毛骨悚然 , 最後一棵樹被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 全世界都是如此 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 對我來說 , 並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到了這麼多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為這個非凡的聰明腦之間 , 是否可能有某種不相干的腦 , 那種ted科技的表現 , 人類的心 ? 用非科學的術語來說 , 談論它 , 以愛和同情的角度來說 , 是否有一些不相干的腦 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們說話時 , 基本上他們既是沮喪或冷漠 , 又或者是痛苦又生氣 。 他們說了更多或多或少相同的話 。 " 我們覺得這樣 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 沒有我們能為它做些什麼 。 "
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我想我們自從他們年紀以來 , 如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我就感到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	導致這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽 , 從坦尚尼亞開始 , 現在已經擴散到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根使得堅定的基礎
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎很小 ; 要抵達陽光──它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆當作我們在地球上所引發的所有這些問題 , 環境和社會 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有成千上萬的年輕人可以打破這個世界 , 讓所有生物都能有更好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人都會造成改變 , 每一天 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇 , 去選擇我們想要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 , 要我們改變事情 , 這樣窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽團體都選擇三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於它們的年齡 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論在城市或鄉村 , 都取決於什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼稚園到大學的程式 , 有越來越多的成人開始自己的根與芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每個團體都選擇 , 在他們之間 , 三個不同類型的計畫 , 來讓這個世界變得更好 , 體認到所有這些不同的問題都互相聯繫 , 並互相阻礙 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的一個計畫將是幫助他們自己的人類社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會募到資金來幫助世界其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物 , 不僅是野生動物 , 還有家居動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	而其中一個計畫將是幫助我們共同的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	這一切都是為了學習生活在和平和和諧之中 , 在我們的家人、社區、文化、宗教和自然世界之間的訊息 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們現在的速度去摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要在非洲挑選一兩個專案 , 即根與芽團體正在進行 , 一兩個專案只在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果巴拉薩維爾、獅子山、喀麥隆和其他團體中 。 正如我所說 , 它是在世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種植樹木 。 他們種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營裡工作 , 帶著雞肉、賣雞蛋 , 只用一點點的錢 , 或只用它們來餵養家人 , 感受到一種驕傲和賦權感 , 因為它們不再無助 , 取決於別人用蔬菜和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 讓士兵們去研究 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的計畫 , 把他們從自己身上帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會的有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄裡也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根與芽的時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 噢 , 他們也致力於愛滋病
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要成份 , 年長的孩子和年紀較小的孩子交談 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而不尋常的懷孕之類的 , 年輕人會聽得更好 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的東西 , 你看過黑猩猩數目減少了大約一百萬隻 , 在本世紀初 , 到現在還不到十五萬隻 , 其他許多動物也一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經有森林的沙漠
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這驚人的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	而我的意思是 , 想想看科技
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我實在太激動了 , 終於來到人們談到堆肥式火箭 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只要把這些水沖到梯子下 , 真是糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	然後談到再生能源拼命的重要性
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否在乎地球給我們的孩子 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們當中有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪女 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們就能做點什麼 。 我們可以做出選擇 , 做為我們每天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買的東西 。 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	而選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 會如何影響我孩子的生命 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或不管是什麼
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以人腦 , 與人心結合 , 我們加入了世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這正是ted所幫助的 , 和幫助我們的人的google , esri正在協助我們在gombe國家公園的繪畫 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 它已經開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你今天下午已經聽過了 , 已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 若我們關心未來 , 我們必須要看到改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由是令人驚嘆的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個絕對被摧毀的地區 , 隨著時間 , 或許還有一些幫助它可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	一個例子是tacare計畫
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴過你 , 看似死去的樹木在哪裡 , 如果你停止駭客 , 你不需要因為有木材 , 那麼在五年內 , 你就可以有一棵三十英呎的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以給予第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
