it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這很鼓舞人心 。 它帶給我的最後一類希望 , 我們在過去兩天中已經聽過這麼多:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種對人的堅定性 , 人類精神的韌性 , 使你認為會被貧困、疾病給打擊的人 , 或其他的 , 都可以把自己從中拉出來 , 有時是有幫助的 , 帶著他們的部分 , 帶著他們的部分 , 改變這個世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看 , 非洲只有一兩個人真正鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出非常長的清單 , 但很明顯的 , 納爾遜•曼德拉 , 從十七年的硬體勞工中興起 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著寬恕的神奇能力 , 讓他能帶領他的國家脫離種族隔離 , 沒有血腥洗澡 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowwa , 在奈及利亞 , 他接下了巨大的石油公司 , 雖然世界各地的人嘗試了最好的 , 但卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是年輕非洲人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天也聽過 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我真的很感謝這個機會 , 再次與ted的每個人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	就在那個年輕女子經營這整個會議中心的最後一個字 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 拿著她的認證 , 她是根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達爾essalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說是幫她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 我非常興奮 , 去認識她 , 看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人在被賦權的時候 , 有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更好 , 真的是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜柯恩在海洋和生活中的塑膠污染上分享了一些艱難的真理 , 還有一些關於如何將我們自己從塑膠漩渦中解放出來的思想 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠等 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:對塑膠污染的堅硬真相
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 我剪斷並縫合在一起 , 作為我過去二十年來的藝術作品的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成2和3d的片段、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	和塑膠一起工作 , 大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它和我們一樣是電子的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我進一步教育我自己一些塑膠 , 我其實意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	這是件壞事 , 塑膠會分解成較小的位元 , 因為它總是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現很多是在海洋環境中
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到太平洋垃圾堆和健身房 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我最初的反應--我覺得這就是很多人對此的反應-- " 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去把這個東西清乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我實際上開發了一個提案 , 要用貨船出去 , 和兩艘破壞漁船的拖網 , 吊車 , 一台晶片 , 一台晶片機器和一台冷門機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	而我的意圖是要走出健身房 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 並開始將塑膠晶片切成一些碎片 , 將它切成磚塊 , 可以被用來當作被開發的社區內的建築材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和實際去過健身房的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 很快地 , 我了解到 , 將它清理得很小 , 相對於全世界每天所產生的環境 , 其實我需要回顧 , 看看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的照片是:我們需要找到一個可以關掉水龍頭的方法 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切割單細胞和可使用的塑膠 , 這些塑膠每天都進入海洋環境 , 以全球的規模來看 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這一點 , 我也意識到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 你試著想像在太平洋中間 , 我學到現在已經有11個健身房 , 可能是世界上五個大洋的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是那個我關心的塑膠的健身房而已它是超市裡的塑膠的健身房
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都包在塑膠上 , 甚至在健康食品市場上 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心的是塑膠和毒素 , 從塑膠滲透到我們體內 , 進入我們的體內 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和其他一群人聚在一起 , 他們都在看這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多計畫正在進行 , 但其中有些非常基本 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	一個是:如果我們在海洋中發現的海洋碎片中有80%到90%都是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不把它稱為是塑膠 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書 , 都是關於永續和綠化的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把某樣東西放進去 , 再也不用再想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	究竟是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 只有不到7%的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的去查看 , 尤其是在塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只能在自閉症下 , 或被捲入 , 或被運到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降低 , 轉變為更少的東西 , 雖然玻璃瓶可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大議題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們看到的另一件事是 , 請大家想想 , 我們把第四個r加到前面的 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 , 三個r , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	不論何時可能 , 都拒絕單一用品和可丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些則是非常古老的學齡 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用的是它們 , 而不是很高興 , 還有超級電腦的容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和我的家人做服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一瓶不銹鋼瓶 , 或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 且你忘了把你的不鏽鋼瓶裝滿水或過濾水 , 和買來的塑膠瓶 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在座的各位說的話我知道你們對這個議題很了解 , 就是這在海洋中是個巨大的問題 , 但這是個我們身為消費者所創造的問題 , 我們可以解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對議題的認知 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案來解決這個問題 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以每當可能時 , 要選擇替代單一塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把幹子的潮汐切入我們的海洋中 , 如此一來 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這位在麻省理工學院的pattiemaes實驗室的展示員 , 帕納•米特利是ted的buzz 。 它是一個可穿戴的裝置 , 可以為深度與環境的互動鋪路 。 想像一下 「 少數報告 」 , 然後一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、界面設計、科技
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattiemaes和panavmetmory第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很有興趣 , 關於我們能否進化或發展出第六感 , 這種感覺會讓我們無縫接觸 , 且容易取得資訊 , 可能存在於某處 , 能協助我們做出對的決定 , 不論我們在哪裡來 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	在座有些人可能會爭論 , 嗯 , 今天的手機已經不是這樣了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted會上遇到一個人 , 這當然是最頂尖的網絡地點 , 你不會握住某人的手 , 然後說: 「 在我拿出手機和谷歌的時候 , 你還能站得住嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你到超市時 , 你站在那兒 , 站在那一大堆不同類型的衛生紙上 , 你不會拿出手機 , 然後打開瀏覽器 , 去一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的衛生紙上哪些是最有生態能力的購買 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以我們沒有容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定下一步該做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	因此 , 我在媒體實驗室的研究小組一直在開發一系列的發明 , 以一種簡單的方式來取得這些資訊 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來到這裡 , 揭開我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 這在過程中還是很有成效 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我現在正在戴著裝置 , 我們已經把它和架子上的零件混合在一起 , 順便說一下 , 在這個時點只有350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著攝影機 , 只是一台簡單的網路攝影機 , 可攜帶電池驅動的投影系統 , 帶著小小的鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件會傳達到我的口袋裡的手機 , 它會作為溝通和計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•密斯蒂 , 他真的是執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走到任何表面上 , 開始用他的手去和他面前投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤這四個顯著的手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個案例中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記蓋子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更時髦的版本 , 你也可以在不同的顏色上畫你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	相機基本上可以追蹤這四隻手指 , 辨識出他製作的任何手勢 , 讓他可以去 , 例如 , 一張長灘的地圖 , 放大等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統也能辨識出具代表性的手勢 , 比如 「 拍照 」 手勢 , 然後拍照在你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以直接走到任何一面牆上 , 投影所有他拍的照片 , 整理出來 , 再次使用全然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 有些人最可能在兩年前來到這裡 , 看到傑夫•漢的示範 , 或者你們有些人可能會想: 「 嗯 , 這看起來不像微軟的表面桌嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢來互動 , 雙手 , 等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別在於你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手如果沒有其他東西是可取得的 , 和這個專案的資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 一個重要的差異是 , 它完全是行動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差異在於 , 在大規模生產下 , 比今天的手機更不費力 , 更不用說是大型的包裝 , 比我在脖子上穿的這個版本還要更時髦 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除了讓一些人活出你幻想中的 「 湯姆•克魯斯 」 , 在 「 少數族群報告 」 中 , 原因在於 , 我們對這個裝置感到非常興奮 , 它真的可以作為第六感的裝置之一 , 讓你對眼前的事物有相關資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以我們看到帕拉夫在這裡進入超市 , 他正在購物一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統就能辨識出他正在拿起的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠光或橘色光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個選擇是特別好的選擇 , 因為他個人的標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能希望衛生紙有最多白化劑 , 而不是最有生態責任的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以拿到亞馬遜的評級 , 在書的封面上得到投影 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順便說一下 , 在亞馬遜的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , pranav把書的頁面打開 , 可以看出更多關於書讀者留言的資訊 , 可能是他最喜歡的評論家等等的資訊 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉到某個特定的頁面 , 他會找到一個註解 , 一個我們朋友的專家 , 讓他有一點額外的資訊 , 關於這個頁面上的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙--它從來不需要過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在讀到的事件的影片註解 , 可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是一個更具爭議性的
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某人互動時 , 也許你可以看到標籤的雲 , 和那人的部落格和個人網頁相關的字眼 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生對相機有興趣等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你前往機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的飛行被延遲了 , 大門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道目前的時代是什麼 , 像在手臂上畫手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	所以 , 這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感 , 可以讓我們無縫接觸到所有相關的資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生panav , 他真的像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確應得了很多掌聲 , 因為我認為他在過去三個月中睡得不多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能對他也不滿意 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不完美 , 它在進步上是很有成效的 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 或許在十年內 , 我們會在這裡 , 最後第六感的植入物 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里格斯和艾瓦菲有個強大的友誼 , 誕生於無法想像的失去 。 羅德里格茲的兒子在2001年9月11日的世貿中心被殺害 ; 艾瓦菲的兒子祖薩烏斯•莫伊被定罪 , 在那些攻擊中 , 為了尋找和平 , 這兩個媽媽媽在2001年9月11日來理解和尊重彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911的療癒:找到寬恕的母親 , 友誼 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲莉斯•羅德里格茲:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們大多數人認為一個不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次了解到 , 我兒子在2001年9月11日的早晨 , 在世貿中心 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否還沒成功 , 直到36小時後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會以我們兒子的名義 , 我丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它 , 然而 , 透過震驚 , 驚恐的衝擊 , 以及我們生命中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們並沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後 , 薩卡利亞斯•莫薩丘伊被指示要犯下恐怖主義 , 美國政府為他命名為死刑 , 如果被定罪 , 我和我的丈夫在公開場合發言 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些和透過人權團體 , 我們和其他數個受害者的家人團結在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 當她的兒子被指控時 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天我想要在我強壯的時候遇見那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲傷中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我立即得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她兒子被指控是什麼時 , 她沒有得到那份同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難等同於我的 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以我們在2002年11月見面 , aicha現在會告訴你這是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是扎卡利亞斯莫薩丘伊之母 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織 , 把我和受害者的父母接觸 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我到五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到了phyllis , 我看著她 ,
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我受苦了很多 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 一個十六歲時的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以關於zacarias的故事實在太多了
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像是他被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否活著 。 我不知道他是否受折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 所以我的苦難對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有女性來說 , 所有賦予生命的母親 , 你可以給予回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	對我們女人來說 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定是手動的 , 一起做些什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女人 , 而是對我們 , 對我們女人 , 為我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我對抗暴力 , 對抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校和年輕、穆斯林的女孩談話 , 讓他們不接受和她們的意願結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以如果我能拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 避免她們結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是我在你們面前的原因
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們和其他家族成員第一次會面 , 這是個非常私人的會議 , 因為當時是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕那個時代的超級暴動主義 , 那些我們家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都如此緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 為什麼她要跟我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們想見她 ? 」

then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們和支持、協助坐落在一個循環中 , 從人們體驗到這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	然後aicha開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是否有罪 , 或無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 對你家人發生了什麼事感到抱歉 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道受苦的是什麼 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該被公平地審判 , 並受罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那樣的方式向我們伸手 , 那時 , 我想說 , 這真是個冰淇淋 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的事 , 我們都說了我們的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束時 , 午餐三小時後 , 我們覺得好像永遠都認識彼此一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 是女人 , 不只在當下的情況下 , 她們可以如此慷慨 , 以及當時的狀況 , 以及她兒子所做的事 , 她們所經歷的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼艱苦的人生 , 來自完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一個特別的連結 , 我非常珍視 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我覺得這一切都是為了害怕對方 , 但讓那一步接著意識到: 「 嘿 , 這沒那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能跟誰見面 , 我不知道 , 還是我和我這麼不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字來做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	伊莎貝爾:我想說 , 我們必須試著認識其他人 , 另一位 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須很慷慨 , 你的心也一定很慷慨 , 你的腦袋一定很慷慨 。

this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多缺乏乾淨飲用水 。 工程師michaelprichard在發明可攜式的壽命過濾器 , 可以讓2009年tedglobal得到最驚人的演示 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、demo、設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水資源、設計、設計、全球性的議題 。
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	michaelprichard的水過濾器會把骯髒的水變成可飲用的水 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都很享受過去幾天在會議上為你們提供的水 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是來自安全的源頭 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果是從這樣一個來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	統計數字會說 , 在座有一半的人會受腹瀉所苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我談了很多關於統計的 , 對於所有人來說 , 安全飲用水的條件 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎無法穿透 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 用目前的思維 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們直接關掉:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	嗯 , 今天 , 我想告訴各位 , 透過不同的思考方式 , 問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	對了 , 既然我一直在說話 , 全世界有1萬3千人現在正在受腹瀉之苦 。
and four children have just died .	而四個孩子剛剛死去
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaverbotle , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的那天 , 我在看亞洲海嘯的毀滅性新聞 , 在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的日子和幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的困住了我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	然後 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風往美國的一邊傾斜 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這裡是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道花了五天才把水送到超級室嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們為了電視設施和水而在街上互相射殺 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定我必須做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 我也在廚房裡 , 到我太太的困擾 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , 救命瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在救命之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以那絕對會穿過那200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救命的孔子是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西能穿透 。

okay . there we go .	好 , 開始了 。

that's all that's necessary .	那都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶打開 , 無菌的飲用水就會出現 。

okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的 。 lifesaverbotle是由全世界數千人使用的 。

and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 使用失敗的技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。

so let's look at the applications .	所以我們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們會怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 在幾週後 , 我們設立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	而人們被迫進入營地 , 以取得他們安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地時 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病傳播 。 更多的資源被要求
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就變成自我延續了 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的思維 , 和運送這些 , 人們可以保持放置 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌的飲用水 , 開始重建自己的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 這不需要自然災害才行得通 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊思維 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 實在太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上執行數字時 , 你就會跑出去 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這裡是 「 思考 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水源 , 使用人造的流程來做這件事 , 讓我們用大自然 。 她有個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡挑起水 , 把水淡化 , 免費運送到那邊 , 然後把它丟到山上 , 河流 , 還有溪流 。

the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的科技 , 在一個jerry罐子裡
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理兩萬五千升的水 ; 這對四個家庭來說是夠好的 , 三年了 。

so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的角度來思考 , 並在使用時處理水 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四個小時來收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的源頭得到
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只要八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧目標 , 讓人們在沒有安全飲用水的情況下 , 就能達到千禧年目標 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	為了將此放入情境 , 英國政府每年花費大約一百兩十億英鎊在外援上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停在那裡 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	只要兩百億美元 , 每個人都可以取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以 , 每年受苦的三十五億人 , 每年死亡的兩百萬個孩子 , 都會活下去 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashown聲稱我們生活在歷史上的一個時刻 , 權力以前所未有的方式改變 。 在tedxbrussels的咒語中 , 他的三個重大的全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashdown:全球權力轉移
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩是由十九世紀末的一位非常著名的英文詩人所寫 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 在邱吉爾的大腦中被說是回聲 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩說: 「 在夏天的愛德蘭山上 , 帶著溪流的流動 , 哈克我聽到了遙遠的鼓聲 , 像夢境中的聲音 , 遠處 , 低音 , 低音在地球的道路上走過 , 親愛的朋友和食物到粉末 , 士兵們很快就去世了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩歌感興趣的人 , 這首詩是《shropshirelad》由a.e.housman所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但豪斯曼所理解的 , 在尼爾森的交響樂中你也聽到了 , 當時19世紀的長期 , 溫和的西爾瓦人夏天來到近距離 , 我們即將進入史上最可怕的時期之一 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些總是月經、女士、先生 , 伴隨著亂流 , 太常出現血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的信息是 , 我相信我們是被譴責的 , 如果你喜歡 , 在歷史上 , 生活的只是那些時刻 , 那些被建立起來的權力順序開始改變 , 而這個世界的新勢力 , 正開始形成形態 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	而這些 , 我們很清楚的看到 , 現今幾乎總是非常動亂的時代 , 非常艱難的時期 , 且太常血腥了 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	對了 , 每一世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你或許會主張 , 最後一次發生了 , 那就是豪斯曼的感受 , 以及邱吉爾所感受到的 , 當權力從舊國度過時 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 跨越大西洋到美國的新興勢力 , 成為美國世紀初期的新興勢力 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 進入真空狀態 , 以前歐洲人的權力被播放了上個世紀的兩場血腥災難 , 第一部分和第二部分:兩場世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經把他們稱為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更精確的形容他們的方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	嗯 , 各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中一次 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 這兩項 , 是關於權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些新的維度我想要參考的 , 這種維度從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 咱們來談談發生在世界各地的權力轉移 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天的情況是 , 在某種意義上 , 令人害怕的 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們見識過希臘的權力轉移到羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力轉移 , 但我們看到了稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅是從國家轉移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今的情況是 , 被納入的權力 , 被告知負責 , 被告知法律規定 , 在國家國家的制度中 , 現在已經大規模地遷移到全球舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們所討論的權力全球化的全球化 , 但其實是真正的權力全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層面上 , 權力的責任歸屬於法律的規則 , 在國際舞台上 , 並非如此 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台 , 權力現在還剩下:網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢改變者的力量──這個廣大的金錢包圍──轉動現在的貨幣數量──對貿易而言 , 應該是要來資助金改變者的數量──如果你喜歡 , 金融推測器 , 已經把我們所有人都帶到膝蓋上 , 近期 , 比起那些發展中國家的預算能力還大了32倍 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個不受規範的全球空間裡 , 不受法律規範的影響 , 人們可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 這讓強大到一會兒 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些擁有最有權力在沒有限制的空間中運作的人 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 更快或更晚 , 不受法律規定的限制 , 不單是你想要國際貿易、網路等等的事情 。 同樣 , 那些你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的東西 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件發生的啟示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些居住於太空的人 , 甚至在你最具代表性的城市--一個九月早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有60%的四百萬美金被拿來資助9•11事件 , 實際上通過了雙胞胎塔的機構 , 9•11事件摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間--大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播者可以繞過它們的毒物 , 也就是破壞我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	更早或更晚 , 更早或更晚 , 歷史規則就是 , 權力的治理必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 正如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的力量 , 那麼它遵循了我們這個時代的挑戰之一 , 就是把治理帶到全球空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的數十年 , 將會是更大或更少的動亂 , 使得我們能達成目標:把治理帶到全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是在說政府
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我指的不是要設立一些全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 我自己的觀點 , 女士們先生們 , 這種做法不太可能 , 是因為推動更多的聯合國機構 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個可以合法化國際行動的手段 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到全球空間的治理時 , 我猜這不會發生在聯合國機構的創作中 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	強大的力量會一起發生 , 做出以條約為基礎的系統、以條約為基礎的協定 , 來管理全球的空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們發生了 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:條約組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到可以容納甚至是最強大的 , 美國 , 如果必要的話 , 就能考量到 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:掙扎的開端 , 來創造一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道我們必須組成一個機構 , 這個機構有能力把治理帶到金融空間給金融推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而g20就是這樣 , 以條約為基礎的機構
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 我們等一下會再回來談 , 那就是 , 如果你把最強大的力量結合在一起 , 以條約制度為基礎的制度 , 填補治理空間 , 那麼 , 剩下的弱者會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們等一下會再回來 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要通過這些亂流的次數 , 或多或少的亂流 , 那麼 , 我們的成功取決於我們的能力 , 將合理的治理帶給全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要跟這樣的觀眾說話 , 但權力不只是垂直轉移 , 它也在水平上轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會主張 , 文明的歷史 , 曾有文明聚集在海邊 , 地中海邊的第一批文明 , 最近在大西洋的西方國家附近才出現 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是權力的根本轉變 , 廣泛來說 , 遠離大西洋的國家 , 聚集在太平洋的廣告牌旁邊 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這從經濟實力開始 , 但這一直都是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增發生在世界上其他成長勢力的國家 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我覺得 , 其實這不是西方轉移到東邊的樣子 ; 不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜想是 , 值得的是 , 美國在未來的十年 , 將會保持地球上最強大的國家 , 十五歲 , 但她所掌握的權力的情境現在已經徹底改變了 ; 它已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們從50年 , 最不尋常的歷史中走出來 , 在這個歷史中 , 我們擁有一個完全獨一無二的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每個羅盤都針對或反對者 , 都必須被它的立場參考 , 華盛頓是一個由一個巨大的競爭者所掌控的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上 , 這種情況並不常見 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是歷史上更正常的情況 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多極化的世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	直到現在 , 美國一直是我們世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強大的國家 , 但他們會是越來越多極化的世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到在中國建立的替代方案中心 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜測是 , 中國對偉大的中心不是平滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	中國在解放她的經濟之後 , 中國將變得更民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論的主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	看到印度 , 看到巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 世界現在看起來 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 更像19世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在十九世紀:一個偉大的英國外交部長 , 坎寧博士 , 曾經形容它為 「 權力的歐洲音樂會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	曾經有一個平衡 , 一個五度的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是對平衡玩耍 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林聯合起來 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供一場反擊 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個壟斷的世界中被支配的時期 , 你已經固定了聯盟 , 北約會 , 戰鬥的act 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力的兩極性 , 意味著修補聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多重權力的兩極性 , 意味著轉移和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們現在所處的世界 , 我們會漸漸看到 , 我們的結盟並不固定 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 偉大的英國外交部長曾說過: 「 英國有共同的興趣 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會越來越明白 , 即使在西方國家 , 我們也必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的合作圈 , 如果我們想把事情做成世界 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家是不夠好的 , 我們必須把其他人帶進去 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方試圖自己去做的時候 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜想是 , 我們已經到達了400年末--我說400年了因為它是鄂圖曼帝國的結尾--西方國家的權力 , 西方制度和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家能一起行動 , 它可以在世界各個角落提出和揭露 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是真的了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的最後一次金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家集合了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金組織解決了問題 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須在他人打電話 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須達到超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你們做個預測 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經達到400年底 , 當時西方的權力足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會參與到世界各地的調停 , 多邊和平的調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔是嗎 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服役 , 在藍色旗幟下服役 , 今天在聯合國的指令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11歲 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大海軍陸戰隊處理索馬利海盜的問題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商人國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想讓海道保持開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	越來越多的情況下 , 我們就得和我們不共享價值觀的人一起做生意 , 但有了誰、誰、當下 , 我們共享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看待現在的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	這是第三個因素 , 這完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們現代的世界 , 由於網路 , 因為人們一直在談論的這些東西 , 一切都與萬物相連 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是互相聯繫的 , 作為國家 , 作為個人 , 以一種前所未有的方式 , 以前從來沒有如此過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關聯性 , 嗯 , 它總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是要管理國家的互聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切關在一起
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 對查爾斯迪加爾機場24小時後會出現問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 整個瓦解
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的步驟中有火災 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地、根深蒂固 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著一個國家獨自行動的觀念 , 而不是與他人聯繫 , 而不是與他人合作 , 不再是可行的主張 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	由於國家的行動不容自身 , 也不足以讓國家自己掌控自己的領土 , 因為國家外部的影響已經開始影響他們內部 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一個小帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的防禦是一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多堅強 , 我們的空軍有多堅固 , 我們的海軍有多堅強 , 以及我們的盟友有多堅強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是當敵人在牆外的時候 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人在牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	如果我想要談談我國家的防禦 , 我必須和健康部長談談 , 因為流行疾病對我的安全是威脅 , 我必須和農業部長談談 , 因為食物安全是威脅我的安全 , 我必須和工業部長談談 , 因為 , 我們的高科技設施的脆弱性 , 現在是攻擊我們的敵人的時刻 , 正如我們從網路戰爭中看到的 , 我必須和家裡的公共事務部談 , 因為在我的國家 , 在我看來 , 在我的家裡 , 曾經發生過什麼事 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是一個國家的安全只對它的士兵和它的國防部的重要性
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	將其制度關在一起的能力
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你一些非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模型上 , 垂直階層 , 專門處理任務 , 指揮結構已經完全搞錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業界知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網絡 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	網絡的能力很重要 , 不論在你的政府或外部 , 都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是阿什肯的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 不要問我關於阿什肯的第一定律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明過這些法律 ; 如果有第三個法則 , 聽起來一定比較好 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三個法則是 , 在現代 , 所有事物都與一切緊密相連 , 最重要的事是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構最重要的一點是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊的登記 , 不論你是生意的 , 是你的碼頭指 , 你的交際官 , 你的能力和他人的網絡 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解 , 在產業中 ; 政府不會 。
but now one final thing .	但現在是最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的情況 , 各位先生女士們 , 我們現在被關起來 , 以前所未有的方式 , 那也是我們彼此的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 這是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 使我們成為國家安全的概念 , 不再足夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前的情況是 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我很安全 ; 我的盟友 , 像北約 , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	已經不是這樣了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	緊密相連性和大規模毀滅性武器的發展 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和敵人分享了命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官在和日內瓦的蘇聯制約協商時 , 在七○年代 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方都意識到零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人共享命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的一個大障礙就是 , 雙方 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦人 , 都不了解他們共享一個集體命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 女士們先生們 , 什麼是遠見和詩人的主張 , 變成我們必須認真看待公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我會用一首
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐恩的偉大詩作 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要把鈴聲傳送給誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是島嶼 。 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它說: 「 每個男人的死亡都會影響我 , 為了我參與人類 , 不要向誰求助 , 請求誰的鈴聲 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對johnonne而言 , 道德的建議
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 對於我們生存的方程式的一部分
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的道路 , danbuetner和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區 」 社區 , 他們的長者與維姆一起生活 , 去記錄年齡 。 在tedxtc , 他分享了9種常見的飲食和生活方式習慣 , 讓他們在一百歲以上都不停地生活 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生活、科學
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	所謂的丹麥雙胞胎研究成立 , 只有大約百分之十的平均壽命 , 在某些生物限制下 , 是由我們的基因所主宰的 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外90%則由我們的生活方式來主宰 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊的前提:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能想出一個事實公式來延長壽命 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食 , 或水墨飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國糧食金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	這是歐普拉告訴我們的 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們的是
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更長久的東西 , 有很多困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是要吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補充品時 , 你該拿它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些激素或反效果呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	有目的嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們找到長壽的方法是與國家地理協調 , 老化的國家研究所合作 , 找到四個人口統計數字確認的地區 , 地理上的定義 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後把專家的團隊帶到裡面去 , 以便通過這些人所做的事 , 把跨文化的幻燈片拆下來 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	在這結束後我會告訴你們那偽裝是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先 , 我想在長壽時解開一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是如果你真的很難活到一百歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有1/5 , 000人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國成長最快的人口統計數字還是很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題在於我們不是為了長壽而寫程式 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被程式設計為一種叫做 「 成功 」 的東西 。
i love that word .	我喜歡那個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家很成功的說詞 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一代 , 當你的孩子有了孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那演化的效果完全消失後 ,
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 都是相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要把它做成一百歲 , 你不只需要有非常好的生活方式 , 你還得贏得基因樂透 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 有九十九件事可以讓我們年齡化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	剝奪了你的腦氧氣僅僅幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太難了 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 毀了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊來槍 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出問題 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 數以兆計的 「 t 」 , 我們在這裡談的是國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就會自轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們轉身時 , 都會有損害 。 那損害會造成 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並以指數型態建立起來 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像當我們都有披頭四的專輯或老鷹的專輯時 , 我們會在錄音帶上複製 , 讓朋友們複製這些錄音帶 , 很快地 , 就能成功的一代 , 錄音機聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有任何東西可以減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體、身體的能力 , 大約是90年 , 女性多一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線的某處 , 我們在桌上留下了大約12年的好處 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年我們可以得到
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 它們會多年免於慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些缺失的年齡 , 最好的方式就是觀察全世界的文化 , 其實正在經歷它們 , 人們活到一百歲以上的年齡 , 比我們高出十倍 , 平均壽命是十倍的十倍 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們找到了第一個藍色區域 , 離義大利海岸約125英里 , 在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島 , 島嶼大約有一百四十萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做nuoro省的地區 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有男性活得最長的地區 , 比美國這裡的百歲人多約十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不但達到100歲 , 還能做到非凡的惡棍 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	十二歲的地方 , 仍然騎腳踏車去工作、砍木 , 且比他們還年輕60年 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實可以追溯到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是青銅時代的文化已經被隔離了 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這片土地是如此的侵略性 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 這種地方會定期、低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎的 , 集中在他們可以帶進田裡的食物 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一種未經釋放的全麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂劇 , 一種由草草製的動物製成的乳酪 , 所以乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 一種來自玉米動物的葡萄酒 , 比世界上所知的葡萄酒含量高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但是真正的秘密--我認為他們是以他們組織社會的方式說謊的 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最瘋狂的元素之一就是他們如何對待老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你曾注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看廣告
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你越年長越有平等 , 你就越能被讚揚的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 卻沒有看過運動示威游泳日曆 , 你看到月曆的百歲人種 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不只對老化的父母有益 , 讓他們和家人保持接近 , 大約四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子而言 , 死亡率較低 , 罹患率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	也就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了第二個藍色區域 , 大約在東京南方八百英里 , 位於okinawa的亞洲 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的基礎 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的女性族群找到的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	一個人們擁有世上最長的殘障壽命的地方
they have what we want .	他們擁有我們想要的
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很久 , 往往會在睡眠中死去 , 很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性交之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	和美國百歲人一樣多的五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	第五次是蟻群和乳癌的比率 , 美國這裡的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	而心血管疾病發生率的六分之一
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而這個文化已經產生這些數字的事實暗示著他們有東西可以教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 滿是蔬菜 , 裡面有很多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃的食物大約是美國人吃的八倍 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更顯著 , 就是他們吃它的方式 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略 , 以免被過度侵犯 , 如你所知 , 在美國是很大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們從小餐盤吃掉 , 所以它們在每個坐著時都會少吃點卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 你在談話時 , 可以無心無意地吃 , 他們在櫃檯服務 , 把食物放走 , 然後把食物帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有一個3000歲的學歷 , 我認為是有史以來最棒的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	是由疑惑所發明的
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	那種飲食被稱為 「 哈蒂 」 、 「 飲食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯之前會說 , 要提醒他們不要再吃 , 當他們的胃滿了80% 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	花了大約半小時的感覺從你的肚子傳到大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要停止百分之八十 , 它能幫助你免於做那件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 如薩丁尼亞 , okinawa有少數幾個社會建構我們可以與長壽相關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致死 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 一般美國人有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在下降到一半
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 出生於okinawa , 你生在一個系統裡 , 你自動擁有半十個朋友 , 和你在人生中旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 莫ai 」 。 如果你在摩艾的房間裡 , 你會預期 , 如果你遇到運氣 , 如果事情惡劣 , 孩子生病了 , 你總是有你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特殊的摩艾 , 這五位女士已經在一起97年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成年人的生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著退休了簡單的椅子 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語中 , 連一個詞都沒有退休 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	反而有一個詞會影響你整個人生 , 而那個詞就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約翻譯過來了 , 意思是 「 早上醒來的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位102歲的凱特大師而言 , 他的ikigai正為這場武裝藝術所攜帶 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫而言 , 每週要捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 國家老化研究所給了我們一個問卷 , 來給這些百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們非常有文化意義的人 , 那些提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這位102歲的女子 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101年半前分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣的感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	然後她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為這是個美好的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們看了明尼蘇達的草原 , 那裡其實有非常高比例的百歲人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口是第七天的改革者集中在加州的倫馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	慣用主義者是保守的方法 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五從日落到日落的星期六慶祝他們的安息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個 「 24小時聖地 」 , 他們稱之為
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽 , 相較於說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女人的壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位老婦人來說 , 他們的壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	不同之處在於男性之間 , 她們的預期壽命比美國人長達11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這個研究遵循了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 而且我認為它是最好的說明了這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異形的社群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一套非常小的生活習慣 , 他們在大部分的人生中都遵守著 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	直接從聖經上取下他們的飲食
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	第一章 , 第一節 , 上帝談到腿和種子 , 另一節是綠色植物 , 可能缺少肉類 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真看待這個聖經 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們有多忙 , 他們在工作上有多大的壓力 , 孩子們需要被開車 , 他們停下一切 , 關注他們的神、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教裡 , 硬線就是大自然走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	而它的力量並不是偶爾完成的 , 它的力量是每週都做一次 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	都不難 。 不需要花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向和其他的冒犯者交談 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到有人在搖吉姆樑 , 或滾動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是他們說他們的下一個天性步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但他們以深刻且可測量的方式互相影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化已經產出了ellsworthwhareham 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellsorthwhareham已經97歲了
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是數百萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商希望六千美元建造隱私圍籬時 , 他說: 「 我會自己去做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他在外面打壓水泥 , 四處繞著水池 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預料的是 , 或許在第四天他最後在手術室裡
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是桌子上的人 ; 那個人做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	97歲時 , 他每個月仍然做20次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•拉林斯 , 十年三歲的現在 , 一隻活躍的牛仔 , 用游泳開始他的早晨 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	而在週末 , 他喜歡在板子上放置 , 丟棄腐爛的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這裡的雙胞胎城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從抬起的重量開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她進入了根深蒂固的顏色 , 1994年的卡迪拉克賽維爾 , 把聖貝納迪諾高速公路撕下來 , 在那裡 , 她仍然是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19次硬體考察 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一一個你會遇過的人 , 他騎著腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠 , 沒有曬傷 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比騎馬爾吉•德頓更為恐怖 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中的共同點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都做些什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們想辦法把它歸結為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自此之後 , 我們又做了兩次藍色的區域探險 , 這些共同的探險家也堅持不懈 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一項 , 我即將要在這裡提一下 , 沒有一項運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們設立自己的生命 , 以便他們不斷地被激發進入身體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這百歲的琉球婦女在地面上起身向下 , 她們每天坐在地上30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每趟旅行到店裡 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友的家裡 , 都會有一個走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以用來做院子的工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想混合一塊蛋糕 , 就用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里跟跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做刻意的身體活動時 , 他們會享受的事物 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一能證明認知衰退的方法 , 他們都傾向於花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來安排他們的生活 , 所以他們有正確的外出 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都要花時間下班 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這種祖先的調查
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你處於危機或壓力之中時 , 會引發一種稱為 「 發炎反應 」 的東西 , 這種反應和所有東西都有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天慢下來十五分鐘 , 你將那個發炎狀態轉變成更反炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有詞彙為目的、ikigai , 像okinawans 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的感 , 他們在人生中啟動 , 這價值約七年的額外預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反的 , 這些人每天都喝一點 , 對美國人口來說不是很難賣 。
