they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向吃以植物為基礎的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表它們不會吃肉 , 而是大量的豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	而他們有策略 , 不受過度過度的侵犯 , 那些在對的時間將他們從桌上奪走的小東西 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	然後這一切的基礎是他們如何聯繫
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和老年父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於以信仰為基礎的社區 , 這在四到十四年間的平均壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的一點是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就生來就是他們主動把自己包圍著對的人
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從franmingham研究中得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友都過胖 , 有50%的機率會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 那會隨著時間產生可測量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友對休閒的想法是身體活動 , 保齡球 , 或打曲棍球 , 騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝一點 , 但不多 , 他們也吃得對 , 他們很投入 , 信任和值得信任 , 這會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 世界歷史上沒有任何飲食可以供應超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動課程通常是一月開始的 ; 通常是十月份完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽時 , 藥丸裡沒有短期修補 , 或其他任何東西都沒有 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做最顯著的事 , 來為你的生活加更多年 , 和生活多年 。 謝謝大家 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水會導電 ; 一扇窗戶從開關轉換到不透明的窗口 ; 一種會讓音樂產生的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡塔琳娜莫塔說:該是玩樂的時候了 。 莫塔帶領我們參觀驚喜和酷的新材料 , 並且建議我們會想出它們的好處 , 就是去做實驗、抽水器和玩樂 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩智能材料
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的爺爺從腳踏車和洗衣機中建立了一台飛天車 , 這樣他才能運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起一輛車 , 但也因為他知道如何建造一輛 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間 , 我們了解事情是如何運作的 , 及如何製造的 , 這樣我們就能建立和修復 , 或至少做出關於要購買什麼的決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這種做法在20世紀的後半就已經失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社群和開放原始碼的模型 , 正在將這種知識帶入我們的生活中 , 我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 帶到零件組成的層面 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的部分 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是什麼組成 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人、自閉症的複合材料 , 會改變形狀、會導電的顏料、會改變顏色、會發光的顏料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨可以讓我們畫電路而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我舉的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 藉由打開這個小燈來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電墨水已經被藝術家使用 , 但近期的發展指出 , 我們很快就能用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一張加密裝置的紙 , 注入無色的光照射粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的水晶體只會在邊緣散發光線 , 這個光線會在我打開燈的時候橫跨整個表面 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	對於這個材料的兩個已知的應用包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱性顏料會在特定的溫度下改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我會把這個放在熱盤上 , 它的溫度只比野外環境稍高一點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它的意思是 , 當內容物冷到可以喝的時候 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	所以這些只是一些普遍所謂的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年內 , 它們會在我們日常使用的物品和技術上出現 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛天車科幻小說的承諾 , 但我們可以有可以改變顏色的牆 , 取決於溫度 , 會捲起的鍵盤 , 窗戶會變成不透明的開關 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是受過訓練的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡談智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何製造的 , 但也因為我相信我們應該對構成我們世界的元件有更深入的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技複合體的了解並不足夠 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難在小量上取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	對於如何使用它們 , 幾乎沒有任何資訊 , 很少有人說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 它們主要存在於交易機密和專利領域中 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	所以 , 三年前 , 凱西•男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個我們網站 , 而任何想加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵他人隨時隨地做出貢獻 , 並集合資源 , 如研究論文和課輔 , 由其他的製造者組成 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型且集體產生的 「 性能化 」 資料庫 , 以智慧型材料為基礎 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要關心智慧型材料是如何運作的 ? 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解和使用的東西最後會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿著的衣服、我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在一個由智慧材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道和了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直都是由tinker推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家和改進的發明家 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 當他們在一篇簡單的方法上發表了一篇論文 , 用來製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬丹•巴克 , 他一直沒有任何化學經驗 , 直到那時 , 讀到這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者太空中進行實驗 , 只用自身的物質和工具來完成 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤麵包機 , 他甚至做了自己的旋渦混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/maker的課程 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦接著在網路上發表了他的成果 , 包括他嘗試過的所有東西 , 沒有用 , 所以其他人可以研究和繁衍它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的主要創新形式是把一個實驗在大學裡的一個設備良好的實驗室創造出來 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重現 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 他自己製作了 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	而現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以拿起他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程和改進 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個我想要提到她的專案計畫的例子 , 是要強調材料的表現特質 , 同時專注於建造者的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 以至於他們教導我們事情如何運作 , 但他們設計中的限制 , 影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以 , 漢娜的手法 , 另一方面 , 是要制訂一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們從預先的限制中解放出來 , 透過教導我們材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅膠帶 , 連結到mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據來自麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究 , 漢娜創作了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布料和墨水的材料 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和其他許多製造者一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都能複製並繁殖它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子產品是最有希望的材料科學的分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以 , 漢娜的工藝作品 , 她分享了她的發現 , 開啟了一系列新的可能性 , 都是美學上和創新的可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們從熱情和好奇心中創造出來 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不傳統的角度來處理問題 , 在過程中 , 發現替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式去做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人用材料做實驗 , 越多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主體 , 只有科學家在乎 , 甚至沒有人在家裡做過任何事 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 對於新興科技有先入為主的知識 , 是確保我們對未來有說服力的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡 , 把門鎖起來 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面和後面的少數車輛 。 但如果車子可以互相分享關於他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算在路上每個人最安全的路線 , 珍妮佛•希爾想像一個沒有意外意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jennniferhealey:如果車子可以說話 , 意外可能是可以避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的一件事 , 但事實上 , 宗教的標誌和好運的魅力 , 出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們知道這件事的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是人們十六歲到十九歲時死亡的主要成因 , 在美國導致死亡的原因 , 其中百分之七十五的意外和藥物或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上擔任年輕的駕駛 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮著 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙正在慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙沒有放慢速度 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個人正在停止 , 死了 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	當時正好是65到0嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在煞車上撞了 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感受到abs跳進來 , 車子還在動 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空軍袋子部署 , 車子完全停了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道那輛車停了 , 我想我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想我們可以藉由讓車輛彼此交流 , 轉變駕駛經驗 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想讓你們稍微想想現在開車的經驗是什麼樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 。 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導向下方 , 部分是看不見的道路 , 在其它的金屬巨人之間 , 以超人的速度進行 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要引導你是你的兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的全部 , 眼睛並不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但之後人們要求你做一些事情 , 比如 , 你想做一個車道改變 , 他們問你做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼光從馬路上拿下來 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停下來看你要往哪裡去 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開車走下路 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全駕駛的方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須選擇 , 我看這裡還是我看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作挑選 , 選擇我們在路上打算要做什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會懷念一些
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到不對或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 。 我相信這點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在科技已經存在了 , 可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了車輛互相交換的資料 , 我們將能看到不只三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 右邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥瞰視線 , 我們將能夠看見車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看見前面車輛的速度 , 看到那傢伙走得多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙要降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算和演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為那不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你怎麼能預測未來 ? 那真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不 。 有了汽車 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路行駛 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	他們經常在出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於不久的將來 , 車子會在哪裡做合理的預測 , 其實並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車裡時 , 有些摩托車騎士來得很可惜 ! 每小時85英哩 , 車道設計 , 我知道你有過這種體驗 , 那個傢伙並沒有 「 走出去 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙大概在路上待了半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英哩後 , 有人看到了那個傢伙 , 當一輛車看到那個傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他的位置、速度、好估計 , 他會持續每小時85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車子會知道 , 因為其他車子會在他耳邊悄悄地說: 「 順便說一下 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓的物品 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 如同在汽車之間分享我們的位置資料 , 只要分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我車上有gps和一台攝影機 , 我對於我的位置和速度有著相當精確的概念 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子位置 , 有點像是 , 以及他們要去哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他車子也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確的知道自己在哪裡 , 並且對其他車子的位置感到困惑 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車彼此分享這些資料 , 會發生什麼事呢 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以確切的告訴你們會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬當模糊估計結合時 , 甚至是輕型交通時 , 當汽車只要分享gps資料 , 我們就把這個研究從電腦模擬中移出 , 移到機器人測試床上 , 上面有實際的感測器 , 裝在這些機器人上:鋼索攝影機、gps , 以及在後備系統中常見的二維雷射儀儀儀儀儀器 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還附著一個不對稱的短距離通訊收音機 , 機器人會彼此交流 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器彼此相處時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 且它們能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在把越來越多的機器人加入混合物中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多的聊天器時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 那就是預測模型協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人汽車都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你不會多注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	優先順序看待一個人 , 似乎有點偏離了 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且可以預測新的軌跡
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他下課了 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道哪些驅動力你需要警醒 , 才能離開 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼做才能讓每個人都保證最好 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車怎麼能竊竊私語: 「 你需要走出路來 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:第一 , 車的能力 , 以及第二個駕駛能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能不會在緊急情況下做出反應最好的位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一系列的研究 , 進行駕駛狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測 , 如果駕駛者要向前看 , 向下看 , 看手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪輛車 , 在最好的位置 , 走出最好的路 , 為每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	從根本上來說 , 這些技術今天就存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個令人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 跟其他車子談我們 , 我們會在一條八卦的大海中沿著路走下去 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種保護我們的隱私的方式來做 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看一下你的車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我覺得這會是件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望各位能考慮一下 , 如果你真的不希望你身後的被分心的青少年知道你在煞車 , 你正要來到一站死去 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由願意分享我們的資料 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子八卦 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路變得更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprizeprizepeterdiamandis談到他如何幫助stephenhawking實現了他的夢想藉由飛往太空的上層大氣層並體驗毫無重量的溫度
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談、太空、科技、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的彼得•戴曼迪斯在grogrek的第零點霍金區 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	在座認識我的人都知道我對打開太空前線有多麼的熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界的專家重力-重力的體驗時 , 真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次透過achonxprize見到他 ,
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 第一個團隊在十天內完成一百個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的 「 基因組一百個個體 」 , 我們將其定序為一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特那次事件的椅子
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是到太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力進入零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 唯一能在地球上體驗zerog的方法其實是用無重力飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛過頂部 , 體重達25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再 , 再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到八、十分鐘的無重力nasa如何訓練他們的太空人這麼久 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這樣做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始運作 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布要飛到史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一家政府機關和一家公司飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這麼做 , 你要殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他也想去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力得到所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下來 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場媒體會議 , 我們宣布要做一場0g拋物線 , 給他25秒的0g 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的好轉了 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼他想去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 是非常動人的 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正面臨著被災難摧毀的風險......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為人類的種族沒有未來 , 如果沒有進入太空的話 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在太空總署內部 , 帶到zerog飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們大約有20個人捐贈了150 , 000美元捐款給和我們一起飛的兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡的幾個tedsters
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一整個er
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監控他的po2 , 他的心跳 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們把一切都設定在緊急情況下 , 天知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 太空梭起飛和降落的地方起飛 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的夥伴艾倫•里奇騰堡小心地把他吊成0g 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那兒 , 【我們讓他去體驗體驗體重不重的情形 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那第一個拋物線之後 , 你知道嗎 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們說去 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實對艾薩克•牛頓致敬 , 漂浮了一顆蘋果電腦 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋有同樣的椅子 , 那位艾薩克•牛頓做的 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七個和第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	而這個男人看起來並不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們活在一個珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們這星球的一生中 ,
please join us in this epic adventure .	請在這個史詩般的冒險中加入我們
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫大衛•鮑林斯基提出了三分鐘驚人的動畫 , 呈現出細胞內的巴士生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我來自一個稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 自從我長大以來 , 在藝術和真理和美的表達中 , 我一直在看 , 在科學界中 , 存在著真與美的表情 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都是美好的美好事物 , 但他們都擁有非常美好的東西 , 像是理想的科學和數學 , 幾乎是科學家會想約會的雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達出真相是可怕的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是很有力的理想 。 它們是不可或缺的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時候是有用的 , 通常是之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	而你現在可以翻翻一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美麗 , 常常對不在科學領域的人不公正 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是描述美麗的事物 , 通常只能在你了解語言和語法時才能夠形容美麗的事物 , 研究對象是哪些真與美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有個人類的理想 , 你可以看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字進化--這些都是非常難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導為父親的動畫以來 , 我試著要做的是 , 他是一位雕塑家和我的視覺導師 , 我想要想出一個方法來協助人們了解生物科學的真相和美 , 藉由動畫 , 用圖片 , 說故事 , 讓人們不見得被帶來的事物 , 並且能夠被教導 , 並且能夠被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 在那裡他們所學習的主題是有真與美的主題 , 嵌入在他們身上 , 但他們被教導的方式是相對的 , 並且被吸引到重點 , 事實和美不見得是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞湯裡的老配方 , 把雞肉煮沸 , 直到口味不見了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這麼做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛大學的robertlue打電話給我 , 在分子和細胞生物學部 , 幾年前 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛大學的醫療和科學教育如何完成 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始了一項計畫 , 來探索那些能夠探索分子和細胞生物學中真相和美麗的細胞 , 讓學生能了解他們所有這些事實的大型照片 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以把細胞的心智影像當作一個大型、正在忙碌、非常複雜的城市 , 由微機械所佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 正是奈米技術人員的羨慕世界 , 自主、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 是由胺基酸的弦所組成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械發電機是如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能發揮細胞的複製性 。 它們能發揮我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們供給我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 我們如何把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 讓它成為哈佛的生物維護中心 , 它是一個哈佛的網站 , 哈佛為它的分子和細胞生物學系學生所做的 , 除了所有文字訊息以外 , 除了所有教學的東西都放在一起視覺化 , 讓這些學生們有了內化的觀點 , 看待細胞真正的真相和美麗 , 並且能夠在心中研究 , 這樣他們的想像力就會被激發出來 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你有巨噬細胞在微血管下串流 , 它們正在觸摸微血管壁的表面 , 它們從毛細管壁上的細胞取得信息 , 它們被給了這些信息 , 在外面某處有發炎 , 無法看見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊 , 導致他們停止 , 引起他們內化 , 他們需要做出各種各樣的零件 , 讓它們改變形狀 , 試著從這個微血管中跳出來 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛的科學家和數據bank模型合作 , 找出它們是如何移動的 , 找出它們是如何運作的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何用真相的方式來實現它所發生的事情 , 但沒有這麼說的 , 細胞裡的交通擁擠會阻礙視覺的發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給大家看的是一部三分鐘的讀者消化版本的這部電影的第一面向 。 它是一個持續進行的計畫 , 將會持續四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望各位看看這個 , 看到細胞製造這些小小的步行機器的路徑 , 它們叫做骨骼 , 將這些巨大的負荷以相對的尺寸挑戰螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	拍電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器非常驚人 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	互相傳遞訊息
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會導致細胞內不同的事發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	而細胞實際上會製造果蠅需要的部分 , 從從細胞核中帶出的信息 , 由分子來判讀基因 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 都有可能沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 沒有這些機器的出席率會很高 , 克里斯 , 非常高興 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送傢伙 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他拉著一個裝滿全新的製造蛋白質到細胞所需要的位置 , 不論是對細胞膜 , 不論是對一個器官 , 不論是用來建造東西或修復什麼 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	而我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西跑來跑去 , 就在你100兆個細胞裡 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你都沒有真正的內在在在做什麼 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家時 , 我希望你能做的事 , 想想看 , 我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看我們正在學習的一些關於細胞機械的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了這一切 , 相信我 , 我們就幾乎知道一旦我們搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠掌控我們對健康做的事 , 用我們未來的世代做的事 , 以及我們將活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個來發現更多的真相 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 非常驚人的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 足以體會到它們所需的細胞 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們同心協力 , 讓細胞做該做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作幫助我們的身體巨大的實體 , 使他們無法正視功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝克•布蘭頓計畫在她的車上住了一年 , 看到了這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症開始了 , 她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅行轉變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她身為美國無家可歸者的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會變革、社會、說故事、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝克•布蘭頓:那年 , 我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是一位作家和記者 , 我也是個瘋狂的好奇者 , 所以 , 在22年當記者時 , 我學會了如何做很多新的事情 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到如何做的事情之一就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了當報紙編輯的工作 , 就在同年二月去世後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死對我來說相當困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我在做這件事的時候 , 有很多我想要感受和處理的事 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都露營了 。 我決定 , 住在旅行車裡一年 , 要這樣做會像是一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包我的貓、我的腐爛推土機和露營裝設備 , 進入1975年雪佛蘭的車中 , 開車進入日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會平等生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一塊留給一個人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到他人的負面感知有多快可以影響我們的現實 , 如果我們放手的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在廂型車很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在校園裡洗澡 。 我定期吃東西 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接下來的憤怒和憂鬱症 , 是我父親的死去 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須全職工作才能支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個溫和的春天變成了一個極度熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	而且在任何地方都不可能停車 , 沒有很明顯的到我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓跑過來 , 穿過車子的一扇開窗
the doggy went into doggy day care .	玩意兒進入了 「 道奇日 」 照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能時 , 我都會在辦公大樓裡使用員工淋浴間 , 卡車停止 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共休息室洗衣服
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	車廂裡的夜空溫度很少下降到華氏80度以下讓睡眠不足或睡不著
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	在我冰冷的胸部在幾小時內就融化了 , 那真的很悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我找不到一間公寓 , 或買不起一間公寓 , 讓我能擁有rotweiler和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣讓我生病時 , 要走五十英尺高的公共廁所 , 晚上我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天的天氣落入時 , 溫度下降到冰凍之下 。 然後他們待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停了一個不同的位置 , 這樣我就能避免被警察察注意到並被警方所綁架 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得自己已經失控了 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但是我從一個有才華的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在旅行車裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 , 我的智商沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、完整性、價值觀 , 所有關於我的事情都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我的確改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我把更深入、更深入的憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我參加了一個無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我已經三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和任何人一樣殘酷和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不喝醉或高度 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當無家可歸的男人了解到 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的 。 你為什麼真的會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我的確如此 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的一種反應 , 讓我憂鬱症自殺 。 我記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了我自己 , 沒人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 在那之後不久 , 她聽到提姆•羅瑟特 , 一個全國知名的記者 , 一直在說我在國家t.v.
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫的一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他去世前一年 , 是在提姆的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做演講的節目電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrusert , 《見報社》的前主持人 , 談到我的寫作 , 當我住在沃爾瑪停車場時 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它到了我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我就站在那裡 , 重新畫了我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後沒多久我搬回田納西
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在旅行車和沙發衝浪間的替代品 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	到了接下來一年的夏天 , 我是工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎金 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再是隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全力工作 , 兼職 , 住在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會繼續汙名化 , 罪犯在你的車上或街上犯罪 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 主要是看不見的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇過一場 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何如果有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來到這裡 , 為無家可歸的海報
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來這裡鼓勵你們把錢捐給下一個你遇見的乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡、睡哪、睡哪裡 , 或是他們在任何時間的人生狀況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在沃爾瑪停車場的車裡 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠 , 總是找到一個方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的《保險套先生》中 , 我用viravaidya , 帶領我們走過全國大膽的計劃 , 提高生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這代表了很多frank、有趣和非常有效的談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	艾奇•維拉瓦迪亞:保險套如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 有許多人生活在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定對此做點什麼 , 但我們並沒有從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭普通的計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的幼兒健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 ,
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:到孩子們 , 去找母親 , 然後跟隨家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩童死亡率 , 你也需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要去做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個孩子的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女性說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會使用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們有非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有得到答案 ; 我們沒有接受這個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士和助產士 , 他們也是女性 , 做了很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很美好 , 但它只涵蓋了全國20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其它80%的人做的事 , 讓他們獨自一人 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找你看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那個黃色標誌下 , 我希望他們沒有消滅過 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂大得多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人就是我們選的那些人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區裡很有名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們是很棒的 , 他們自己也在做家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應藥丸和保險套 , 在全國的每個村落 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以我們就在那裡 , 我們去找那些被視為是問題的成因 , 成為解決方案的成因 。

over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過四分之一的一百萬人被教導關於家庭規劃的新字母a , b代表生育 , c代表保險套 , 我是為了ud , 投影片 。

uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 。 先動一下 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉了 , 不用保險套 , 再來 , 再來 。 」

in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會讓它變成保險套是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個微型貸款計畫 , 組織它的女性說: 「 我們只想借錢給實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們那裡拿出一筆貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	經過35/36年 , 還在持續下去 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真的銀行 , 但它是資助的微型貸款 。

and this is on the fourth of july .	而這是在七月四日 。

we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校的所有冰箱中都有保險套 , 因為酒精的損害會造成判斷 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是企業家 , 缺乏商業技能和信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是由商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小商人 。

so , that was done .	所以 , 實現了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	經費從公司進入村落 , 透過樹木栽種 。

and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	而在你能借錢之前 , 你需要接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 信用的人一定是人權 。

otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫貧 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在收到貸款之前 , 你一定要被訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	以下是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就成功了 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	最後 , 在教育方面 , 我們希望能把學校改造成一個地方 , 讓每個人終身學習中心 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會感覺好像朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你一陣子 , 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•狄摩斯 , 智慧型手機的迷你機器人 , 可以跟你一起走路 , 滑動你一杯咖啡 , 用可編寫的表情來回應你 。

and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 那真的是很困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不但能真正負擔得起 , 而且必須是人們真的想要帶回家 , 帶著他們的孩子去 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這種機器人不能令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善和可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個機器人 , 用你已經知道且喜歡你的iphone當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一個機器人 , 可以用wi-fi和電腦視覺來支付150美元 , 這大約是過去這類機器人花費的百分之一 。

that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給祖母 , 住在國家的另一端 。
