but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想透過談我們未來正在努力的事情來結束 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一位工程師 , dom , 在一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它建在google開放的架構上 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖著和放下這些積木的塞滿密碼 , 為你想要的機器人創造出任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	而實際上你可以在瀏覽器中模擬那種行為 , 也就是你看到romo在左邊做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有自己很驕傲的東西 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些wi-fi實現的機器人實際上彼此互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注在打造機器人 , 每個人都能訓練的原因 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人身上 , 最有說服力的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人轉變為人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為 , 如果你家裡要有機器人 , 那機器人應該要成為你自己的想像力的表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我完全不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美元 , 或一個大型的人類機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它會依賴小型、敏捷的機器人 , 像romo這樣的機器人 , 以及像你自己這樣的人的創意 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們等不及要讓你們所有機器人 , 我們也等不及要看你們建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 在這場演講中充滿熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、婦女、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德告訴熱情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	謝謝大家 。 在這裡非常可怕 , 最聰明的一面 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴你們一些熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我很喜歡
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事的人 。 我想傳達一個比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我感興趣 , 有些讓我痛苦 , 直到我最後寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫下關於巧合、準備、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直住在匿名度 , 直到2006年2月 , 當我在義大利的冬季奧運會上載奧運旗幟 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在人們在macy's認可我 , 我的孫子們都認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	允許我告訴你我的四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧運典禮的組織者之一 , 開幕典禮 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗手之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回覆說 , 這肯定是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我盡可能從運動員的身分得到的程度 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以在體育館裡四處走動 , 沒有步行器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這無關歡笑 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這會是第一次只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 還有三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一輛制服 , 她說 , 並要求我的衡量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己身處富裕的動脈 , 看起來像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我發現自己在圖林 , 在那裡 , 熱情的群眾在八十名奧林匹克隊的任何隊伍都在街上歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏得勝利 , 但還有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	雪的一小點 , 一英吋的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 比訓練或運氣更重要的是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都與熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅色海報報報導宣布奧運會的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 。 難道不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這是我在書裡的角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks、異議人士、冒險家、局外人和反抗者 , 他們問問題、彎曲規則 , 並冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人並不會做有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了另一位旗手:三位運動員 , 主演sarandon和sophialoren 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有 , 兩位有熱情心的女性:waangarimaathai , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主種植了三千萬棵樹 。 藉此 , 她改變了土壤 , 天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然還有很多村莊的經濟條件 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	也是柬埔寨的激進份子 , 他熱切地對抗兒童妓女 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 她祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們小女孩 , 被男人強暴 , 她相信和很小的處女做愛會治癒她們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而有些妓院 , 孩子們每天被迫接到五、十五名客戶 , 如果他們反抗 , 就會受到電力折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到制服的綠色房間裡 ,
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種服裝 , 但離米其林人裝的很遠 , 其實我預期的不是壞事 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但大部分的旗手 , 除了蘇菲雅羅倫 , 美麗和熱情的普遍象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過七十歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很滑 , 很高 , 有很深的水槽 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你怎麼可能有很深的水槽 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視面試中問到: 「 她怎麼可能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背部總是直的 , 我不會製造老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡有一些免費的建議來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不吵雜 , 不咳嗽 , 不吵鬧 , 不跟自己說話 , 不做任何不好的 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育館的翅膀 , 大聲說出者宣布奧林匹克旗 , 音樂一開始 , 同樣的音樂從這裡開始 , 愛迪亞大遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一英尺 , 不是在算毛髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走過 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿 , 肩上拿著旗幟 。 我在我伸展手臂的尖端拿著旗幟 , 這樣我的頭其實是在該死的旗幟下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的相機都是 , 當然 , 在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說是幸運的 , 因為在我出現的大多數媒體照片中 , 雖然常常在蘇菲雅的腿間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都很想成為的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘都是在奧運會場的那些 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我丈夫被冒犯了 , 當我說這句話時 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們在私人身上所做的事通常要花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自接受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四個壯麗的分鐘內所有的壓克力 , 因為我不想忘記 , 年齡破壞了我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是激情的故事
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	1998年 , 這個地方是剛果難民的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上有80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為剛果一個死亡營地 , 因為那些沒有被殺死的人會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•圖迪歐 , 她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們強迫她看著她丈夫被折磨和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她想辦法讓七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生出了早產 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用一根棍子把麻木線切開 , 用她自己的頭髮把它綁起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把雙胞胎命名為在營地的指揮官以獲得他們的利益 , 用黑茶餵食他們 , 因為她的牛奶不能維持下去 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵們在她的牢房裡爆發強暴她最年長的女兒時 , 她會抓住她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使當他們拿著槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了十六個月 , 然後 , 藉由非凡的運氣 , 和一位年輕的美國人的熱情心 , 薩莎.查諾夫 , 他想辦法把她安置在美國救援機中 , 羅西.馬圖迪歐和她的九個孩子最後到了亞利桑納州鳳凰城 , 他們現在活著 , 茁壯成長茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	地圖迪歐 , 在斯華西里 , 意味著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是強壯且熱情的女性 , 像是蘿絲圖迪歐 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們構成 , 不需要這些 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處看到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古時 , 在世界末期 , 在父權天主教和保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪五歲時我是個憤怒的女權主義者雖然這個名詞還沒達到智利所以沒有人知道我到底出了什麼問題
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 要為我的自由付出很高的代價 , 且要質疑父系 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出 , 因為對於我收到的每一次吹風 , 我都得以遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒保拉在她二十歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒和所有人一樣的特權女性 , 今天在座的各位 , 但對世界上其他大多數的姐妹而言 , 她們仍然被迫過早婚、賣淫、強迫勞動她們有孩子 , 她們不想要 , 或無法供養 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們對自己的身體或生活沒有任何控制權 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴 , 被毆打 , 有時被殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大部分西方的年輕女性 , 被稱為女性主義者是侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感過 , 但讓我向你保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我也因缺乏男性而感到無比的痛苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死去 , 沒有意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 為女神的sake 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為aphrody , 或金星 , 或bimbo , 或任何你想要的東西 ; 名字不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個充滿熱情的故事 , 這一個很令人難過 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉的一個小婦女診所
the year is 2005 .	在2005年 ,
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫衛生學家 , 在她的三週假期間 , 去了診所當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備要清潔牙齒 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一排已經等了好幾個小時的婦女來接受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人處於突破性的疼痛之中 , 因為她有數個腐爛的腫瘤 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮了解到 , 唯一的解決方案就是拔掉不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有為此授權 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒很多險 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些非vocaine 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢和熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她衝動一名禱告 , 帶著手術前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 緩解的病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生人員抽出更多的牙齒
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她又來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人在等著她和丈夫一起等著 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女子的臉看起來像個水燈 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它是如此的腫脹 , 甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她做過的事感到害怕 , 但之後翻譯解釋 , 病人的狀況和操作無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打她 , 因為她沒有時間準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬女性像這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性在世界的勞動力上做三分之二 , 但她們擁有不到世界資產的百分之一 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於男性 , 薪水低於男性 , 如果他們有薪水 , 他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	賦予婦女教育、工作能力、控制自己的收入、繼承、擁有財產的能力 , 讓社會受惠 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦權 , 她的孩子和她的家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落繁榮 , 最後整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村落
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和那些婦女談話 , 並解釋土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們已經砍伐並賣掉樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們種植新的樹木 , 用滴水 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	不論五、六年 , 他們都有一片森林 , 土壤都豐富 , 村莊也被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最後退的社會總是那些把女性放下去的 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個明顯的事實卻被政府忽視 , 也被慈善事業忽視 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊美金給一個婦女計畫 , 二十塊美金給男人的方案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們力量 , 將會改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起合作 , 連結 , 知識和教育 , 能為這個弱勢星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 他們是對立的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們所擁有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 在那裡 , 生命被保存下來 , 生活品質很豐富 , 不只是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月 , 我看到費南多•鮑特羅的畫作在加州大學柏克萊圖書館展出 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了帶著波特羅的作品以外 , 沒有任何博物館或畫廊 , 都敢展現畫作因為主題是阿布格拉伊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是一幅巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 在豐富的botero風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的腦海或心裡得到那些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是 「 不當 」 的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕權力濫用 , 以及虐待的權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並迫使其餘的群體接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時會改變 , 但它們總是對它們有益 , 在這個例子中 , 所謂的 「 萬能效應 」 , 在經濟學上行不通 , 完全行得通 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待的訣竅從梯頂往下爬到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和小孩 , 尤其是窮人 , 在最底層
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是男人最缺乏的人他們也能虐待女人或小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了 , 少數人透過性別、收入、種族、階級來執行的權力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 在我們文明的基礎上 , 要做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對於真正的改變 , 我們在世界的管理階層需要女性能量 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要在權力位置的關鍵數量女性 , 我們需要培育男性內心的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的是有年輕人心智的男人 , 當然
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙毫無希望 ; 我們必須等他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想有蘇菲亞羅倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若要有選擇 , 我寧願有旺加里馬塔伊的戰士心 , 索馬利夫人 , 珍妮和蘿絲瑪蒂 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要把它做好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡所有的知識、能源、人才和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們脫離我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 充滿熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦的大小中 , 有三千萬份餐點被服務 。 但所有的食物都來自哪裡 ? 建築師卡洛琳•鋼鐵探討餵飽一座城市的日常奇蹟 , 並展示出古老食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡洛琳鋼:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	如何養活一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的偉大問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為 , 如果我們進入一間商店或餐廳 , 或在大約一小時內進入這間戲院的噴霧器 , 那裡將會有食物在等待我們 , 神奇地來自某處 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 倫敦的每一天 , 足夠的食物必須產量、運輸、買、賣、煮飯、吃飯、丟棄 , 每天都會發生類似的事 , 對地球上的每個城市而言 , 都是很了不起的 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的東西 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃東西 , 我們其實跟我們古老的祖先一樣依賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們更多人搬進城市 , 越多自然世界被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 像我身後的那一塊黃豆田 , 在巴西的馬托格羅索 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些都是非凡的景觀 , 但我們當中少數人能夠看見它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	漸漸地 , 這些景觀不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們更多人搬進城市 , 更多人在吃肉 , 所以現在全球每年有三分之一的穀物被餵給動物 , 而不是給人類吃 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物才能餵飽人類 , 如果它是先通過一隻動物 , 那就不是很有效率的餵食方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個更加嚴重的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 據估計 , 我們人口的兩倍會住在城市裡 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時也估計有兩倍以上的肉類和乳類消耗
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉和都市主義都在手上升 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	那將會帶來巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 60億的飢餓食肉食性食物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 實際上如果我們身為人 , 這個問題很不可能解決 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九百萬公頃的雨林喪失 , 創造新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時我們也失去了等量既有的可耕地 , 以至於鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要10卡才能生產出我們西方消費的每一卡路里食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管有食物 , 我們的生產成本很高 , 但我們其實並不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前有一半的食物被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這漫長的過程結束時 , 我們甚至沒有妥善地管理供應食物給地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人過胖 , 更遠十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有一個是很合理的 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	而當你認為現在食物的全球貿易中有80%是由五個跨國企業所掌控的 , 這是一張很嚴峻的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 一萬年前 , 我會說 , 要回答這個問題 , 是這個過程的開端 , 在東方的古老地區 , 稱為 「 肥沃 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它的形狀是近期的 。
and it was also fertile .	而且它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前就在這裡 , 兩種非凡的發明 , 農業和都市主義 , 大約發生在同一個地方 , 同時發生在同一個地方 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是有限的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為我們古老的祖先首次發現了穀物 , 產生了足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久居住 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些居住地是什麼樣子 , 我們會發現它們是完整的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被有生產力的農田所包圍 , 被像烏爾這樣的大型神殿所支配 , 實際上 , 靈性化、中央食品分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是神殿 , 整理收穫 , 聚集在穀物中 , 將之送給神 , 然後提供穀物 , 讓神不吃東西給人民 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的所有靈性和實體生活都是由穀物所主宰的 , 以及維持它們的收穫 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	而事實上 , 每個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在西元前一世紀有約一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼回饋的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古老的食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬能接觸到大海 , 讓它可以從很遠的距離進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這在古代世界是唯一可行的方法 , 因為在道路上很難運送食物 , 這種方法很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地將戰爭投入在像嘉年華和埃及的地方 , 只為了在他們的穀物儲備上拿到爪子 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張真的是一大段時間 , 把軍事化的購物速度拿出來 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下這個:羅馬實際上是從倫敦來的入口牡蠣的 , 在一個階段 。 我認為那是非比尋常的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過它的胃口塑造了它的印度 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它來自泰姆斯 , 沿著這張地圖的下方 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場到了城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	而這些道路從它們變成便宜的道路 , 也就是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚類也是一樣 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是從河裡進來的 。 同樣的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然billingsgate , 出名的是倫敦的魚市場 , 在這裡運作直到1980年代中期 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真是太不凡了 , 真的 , 當你想到
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都帶著手機遊走 , 看起來像是磚塊 , 還有一些神秘的魚在港口上發生 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市裡另一個關於食物的東西:一旦它進入城市的根源被建立起來 , 它們很少會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是非常不同的故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉都來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達西北區的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 位置在那兒 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	積極是從東安格利亞進來的 , 到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女人在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥兒們的腳被保護著小型的畫布鞋 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們碰到便宜的東邊末端時 , 那是他們被賣掉的地方 , 這就是為什麼它叫做 「 家樂 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看工業時代前建造的任何城市地圖 , 你可以追蹤進來的食物 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物塑造的 , 兩者都是藉由閱讀街道的名字 , 給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在之前的人生中 , 是你到星期五去買你的魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但也必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共場所是唯一能買到和販賣食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年的史密斯菲爾德的影像 , 你可以看到 , 要在這樣的城市中生活是非常困難的 , 且不知你的食物來自何處 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期天的午餐 , 它的機率在你窗外打氣或流血 , 大約三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年偉大的西方國家的影像 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以 , 突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被屠殺於視力和心智 , 在鄉下的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並藉由鐵路進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	而這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首先 , 要讓城市成長 , 任何大小和形狀 , 任何地方都有可能成長 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去城市被地理限制住 ; 他們以前必須透過非常困難的實體手段取得他們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們就有效從地理學中解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	從這些倫敦地圖上可以看到 , 在火車來襲後的九十年間 , 從一個很容易餵食動物的小塊塊狀物 , 到大塊的噴霧物 , 那會非常、非常難餵飽任何人 , 不論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是個開端 。 火車到來之後 , 這真的是這過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最終解放 , 來自任何明顯與自然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這種城市是沒有氣味的 , 沒有混亂的 , 明顯地 , 沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們拿到食物的做法是他們上了車 , 開到外表的某個盒子裡 , 回來後 , 一週的購物價值 , 然後想著 , 地球上該怎麼處理 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的是我們和食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物曾經是中心 , 周邊的城市的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	曾經是社交活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 ; 現在我們只要加水 , 或一點點蛋 , 如果你在做蛋糕之類的 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只要在一個包子上讀到標籤的後面
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不相信它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是貶低它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品食品系統的最諷刺之處之一 , 是他們承諾要讓更容易變得更困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由在任何地方建立城市 , 它們其實已經讓我們與最重要的關係密不可分 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	它們也讓我們依賴的系統 , 只能傳遞出去 , 如我們所見 , 無法永續發展的系統 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯更多人在問自己
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他書《烏托邦》的前線人物 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	當時是一系列的半獨立城邦 , 如果那聽起來很熟悉 , 一天的走向 , 每個人基本上都是耕種馬 , 然後在他們的後花園裡種植蔬菜 , 一起吃共用餐等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本訂單原則 , 儘管有更多人從來沒有這樣框架過它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常著名的 「 烏托邦 」 願景 , 伊比尼茲霍華德 , 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半獨立城邦 , 小小的都會區 , 附近有可耕地的土地 , 由鐵路連接到彼此 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的順序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被打造了 , 但和默斯克韋茲的願景沒有任何關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦的想法的問題就是 , 他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是一個湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為希臘的衍生物有雙重衍生物 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它能不是意味著一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 。 這是個想像的東西 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類潛在的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是西托邦 , 從古希臘語 , 「 西托斯 」 為食物 , 和 「 湯波斯 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經生活在西托邦
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物塑造的世界裡 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以把食物當作一個真正強大的工具--一個概念工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 西托邦可能是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得這看起來有點像
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 。 這只是狗的臉上 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是生活中心的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被慶祝 , 被享受 , 人們花時間來慶祝 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是食物在我們的社會應該在的地方 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不能有這樣的景象 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	對了 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 想到前方的 , 他們會計劃 , 可以盯著一堆原始的蔬菜 , 實際認出他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為 , 若沒有這類的人 , 我們就無法擁有像這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這個 , 因為那是男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路 , 當地食物被種植的市場 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為 , 若沒有這樣 , 你就不可能有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 且不只是一個不可見的零和商品 。
cows with a view .	帶著觀點的牛 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆積的humus
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上就是把整件事情結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們被告知所有的食物 , 並種植自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一種叫凱文的植物 , 也許是屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類試圖將我們與大自然重新連結起來的計畫極其重要 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 西托邦 , 對我來說 , 真的是種看待方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到西托邦已經存在於各處的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅在於加入他們 , 用食物作為看待的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們會停止把城市看成是大型、大都市、不生產的大塊 , 就像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 作為有生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是不可避免的一部分 , 共生的連結 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是一個很棒的圖像 , 因為我們需要不要再這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更加思考永續發展 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖像能為我總結出我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	重新看待食物如何塑造我們的生活 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像來自650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是ambrogiolorenzetti的 " 好政府的忠告 "
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市和鄉間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧了國家 , 國家就會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要我們問 , 如果他今天畫了這張圖 , 會是什麼模糊的 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好政府會變成什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	它是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的東西
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解到 , 世界也是我們吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為一個真正強大的工具來塑造這個世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	從憲章發起 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯在21世紀探討宗教的角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 還是它會讓我們團結共同的好事 ? 她會審查那些可以驅使世界的信仰重新發現黃金法則的催化劑 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009、暴力、暴力
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重新修正黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直覺得很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我開始敏銳地意識到在世界主要的信仰中 , 同情心的中心性 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都演化出他們自己的版本 , 稱為黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它會出現在一個正面的版本 「 永遠對待所有其他人 , 如同你想被對待自己 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 " 不要對他人做你不希望他們做的事 "
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看自己的心臟 , 發現什麼讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 都要對任何人施加這種痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來不錯 , 也因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則時 , 如同康西斯所說的: 「 一整天 , 日復一日 」 , 不只是一個做好事的疑問 , 然後回歸到貪婪和自負主義的人生 , 一整天 , 一整天 , 你把自己從世界的中心 , 放到另一邊 , 你超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶領你進入了所謂的神、涅盤、拉瑪、泰羅的存在 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的自我背景 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來沒有聽過這句話 , 這對宗教生活是如此的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 常常當宗教人士團結起來時 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 他們爭論的是abstrustruse的教條 , 或說說是仇恨的議會 , 或是對同性戀的審查 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和宗教人士談話時 , 有點像個突變的表情 , 跨過他們的臉孔 , 因為人們常常想對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我對ted這麼感激呢 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書籍研究中帶領我進入21世紀 , 讓我能和一個比我想像中更廣泛的觀眾說話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們沒有辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們就對待所有人 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 都跟我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代的偉大任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性的社會 , 如同我說的 , 人們可以在和平中生活在一起 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教反而被視為問題的一部分
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 這不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這個充滿同理心的想像力的舉動 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 對我來說 ,
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們要麼繼續帶出去 , 要麼強調我們信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 要麼我們回到拉比 。 拉比希爾 , 更古老的耶穌的現代人 , 當一個普根人在一站時 , 總結出整個猶太人的教義時 , 說: 「 這對你來說是討厭的 , 不要對你的鄰居做 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉h和其他一切都只有留言權 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教堂早期的拉比人和早期的父親都說 , 任何用來詮釋仇恨和歧視的經文都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要復甦那個精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只是因為愛情的精神使我們崩潰 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切實現 , 我們可以用ted所介紹的現代溝通來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有伴侶的反應感到極大的滿意 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人要用憲章來治癒分裂 , 最近在新加坡社會中已經擴大 , 議會的一些成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家將帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 向他們展示 , 同情心也屬於所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區都在舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰中同情心的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那兒 。 它不能用發射來停止 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 這是我們錯過的地方 , 專注於相信abstrustrines的教條 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定永遠會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	直到我死去的那天 , 我打算要努力 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續跟我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 來教育並刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們已經從同情心下降了 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們經常認為 , 這只是對某人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不了解慈悲 , 如果你只想一想 ,
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 協助解決一些我們對其他人的刻板印象 , 把我們從彼此的角度分開 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣適用於教育家
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能感受到動態、充滿同情生活方式的動態和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它要求敏銳的智慧 , 不只是一種美味的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想呼籲學者 , 用他們自己和其他人的傳統來探索同情心的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許 , 更重要的是 , 要鼓勵對不寬容的演講的敏感性 , 這樣一來 , 因為人們有這份憲章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏信仰 , 他們都覺得有力量去挑戰不寬容的言論 , 不受宗教領袖、政治領袖 , 來自工業界的船長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過把憲章放到網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍舊被困在舊世界裡 , 一大堆的鮑菲斯坐在一間房間裡 , 還在發出另一種阿卡尼聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted介紹了我一個全新的思考方式和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted如此美好的東西 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們加入全部一起 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎是無法避免的 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但最後我想引用一段對英國作者的參考 , 一位牛津的作者 , 我不常引用c.s.路易斯的話 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 自從我讀書的時候 , 我就讀過了 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的《四個愛》書中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他區分了愛情 , 當兩個人凝視、咒語 , 到彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友誼比較 , 當兩個人站在一邊時 , 肩並肩 , 他們的眼睛固定在一個共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	在我們在vey的小說中 , 我強烈感受到 , 當各式各樣的說服者聚在一起 , 一邊為共同的目標努力 , 一邊融化 。
and we learn amity .	而我們學到了野心 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學著一起生活 , 去認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay將風力發揮 , 有時是超現實的旅程 , 走向羅馬學派的完成之旅 , 他的說明向歷史城市致敬 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	macarthurgant、藝術、書籍、城市、溝通、文化、設計、娛樂、幽默、講故事
i draw to better understand things .	我畫畫來更了解事物 。
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時候我會畫很多圖畫 , 我仍然不了解我在畫什麼 。
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	在座的各位 , 對於數位事物感到舒服 , 甚至對那段關係感到羞恥的人可能知道 , 最為人所知的 「 事物運作的方式 」 , 同時準備了一部分名為 「 理解 」 的專輯 , 花了兩天的時間 , 試著讓他的筆電和他的cdburner溝通 。
who knew about extension managers ?	誰知道延伸經理 ?
i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直都在管理自己的延伸 , 以至於我從來沒有想過要讀那些指令 , 但我終於想通了 。 我必須想通 , 因為隨著邀請來源 , 恐嚇的提醒 , 沒有投影機 , 所以 , 把那些卡蘿爾人不再是必要的 , 但有些其他的溝通形式會 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我已知的事物 , 特別適合許多專業人士 , 或者我可以談論我真正關心的事物 。
i decided to go with the latter .	我決定跟後者一起去 。
i'm going to talk about rome .	我要談談羅馬 。
now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	為什麼我會特別在意羅馬 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我在60年代的後半去了羅德島設計學院 , 研究建築 。
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 去年 , 第五年 , 在羅馬當學生 。 這改變了我的人生 。
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	並不是最不理由的 , 是我過去四年都住在家裡 , 每天開車到rsid , 開車回來 。
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了60年代 。 我讀到他們 ; 我了解他們很有趣 。 我錯過了他們 , 但我的確在羅馬渡假了那非同尋常的年度 , 也是離我不遠的地方 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 不論何時給予機會 , 我都會試著用它或它來做點什麼 。
i also make drawings to help people understand things .	我也畫圖來幫助人們了解事物 。
things that i want them to believe i understand .	我希望他們相信我了解的事物 。
and that's what i do as an illustrator , that's my job .	這就是我作為一個插畫家所做的事 , 那就是我的工作 。
so , i'm going to show you some pictures of rome .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些羅馬的照片 。
i've made a lot of drawings of rome over the years .	這些年來我畫了很多羅馬的圖畫

i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層剝去 ; 我們把它們當成一頁 , 用某種方式來做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是層層次的地平層 , 垂直層次 , 我想 , 如果我讓你們想 , 如果我用正確的方式 , 可以讓我看清楚它的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部分建築物的牆壁上覆蓋著疤痕 ; 數世紀以來 , 隨著這些結構的傷疤已經被適應 , 而不是被撕下來 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你直接展開它 , 你就會看到它背後的我所謂的疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造更小的窗戶變得很重要 , 因為壞人來了 , 或其他的 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應所有人都被埋在斯多哥下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這張palazzo的頁面剝出來 , 讓大家看一下裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我還可以向各位展示在其中一棟壯麗的建築物的角落 , 有著巨大的石塊 , 或者是用磚塊和斯特科做的假石塊 , 比較常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以變得稍微立體一點 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你下一條狹窄的小街 , 走進其中一條令人驚訝的皮亞薩斯 , 利用雙重的摺疊雙層摺疊頁 , 如果你和我一樣在小時候讀過一本彈出的書 , 你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭包起來的頁面包起來 , 在這短暫的時間內 , 會出現在那個廣場上 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我沒有做過任何比製作摺疊頁更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但我接著想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神廟和皮亞薩•戴拉•羅頓達在它面前 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這裡有一本完全開放的書
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不把書全部打開 , 如果我把它打開90度 , 我們就在萬神殿的前面向下看 , 我們會看著頂部 , 多或少在廣場上 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把這本書轉向另一種方式 , 我們在萬神殿前面看過正方形 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有折疊 , 沒有把戲 , 只是一本書沒有全部打開 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有前景 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺痕和唯一一部分的開放書做結合 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們進入萬神廟 , 它會成長等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我站在正確的軌道上 , 但它似乎失去了它的人類特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以我回到了故事的概念 , 如果你想讓人們注意一本書 , 一路上收到信息 , 這總是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 讓我震驚的是 「 抓到的標題 」 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是溫和的鴿子 , 會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果標題有用 , 使用它 。 但這會是一段歷經羅馬的旅程 , 展示了所有我喜歡的關於羅馬的事情 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	是一隻鴿子坐在教堂上方
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天掉下來 , 做正常的鴿子 。 回來 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網絡覆蓋 , 這隻鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 還得找另外一個住的地方 , 這讓我可以通過我最喜歡的東西目錄 , 我們從最高的鴿子...等等開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人一起生活 ; 這並不總是件好事 , 但它確實能把鴿子帶在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該要以某種方式參與這件事 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方 , 讓他們有危險的地方 , 他們會和這個傢伙交朋友 , 學會為他做戲法 , 在午餐時間娛樂他 , 等等 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	有一個真正的鍵結在這個老人和這些鴿子之間發展
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時真的生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他被教導要拼寫他的名字 , 也就是aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三四天後出現 , 沒見到他 , 他住在這個小垃圾桶裡 , 他們拼了他的名字 , 四處飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	最後他終於得到足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬上屋頂 , 所有的鴿子 , 一個紅色的氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 把他帶到城市的牆壁上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提這個:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城市牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在老羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有被埋在牆壁裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我想這真的是個歡呼的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	無論如何 , 我經歷了...再一次 , 如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事沒有去任何地方 , 我只是想出了標題 , 希望標題會有點像把我踢向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它的確夠專注 , 我甚至會做個標題 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題的頁面 , 最終引領我到我安定的解決方案 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她在羅馬城牆外傳遞一則訊息給在城市中的人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正飛越appian的上方 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墓頭和松等等的樣子 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你可以看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它變得很有必要且有可能 , 試圖傳達出那種感覺 , 不用實際移動就可以飛過城市 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	越過克西斯提烏斯金字塔──這些對你來說似乎很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬渡過這座大樓 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的東西 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件事情 , 大部分的鴿子都沒做的事:牠要走這條路線 , 這是我感覺到的裝置 , 要把這本書延伸到大約四頁以外的地方 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們圍繞著競技場 , 越過聖母堂 , 位於cosmedin的聖母堂 , 以及海克力士朝向河的神殿 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和palazzofranese設計的這個角落碰撞 , 由米開朗基羅所建造的石頭 , 由競技場狹窄的逃離所拍攝 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們從campodefiori上俯瞰了campo.
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為它是一個完整的標準化 , 否認任何規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點規則是 , 如果它看起來可信 , 你已經成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著搞清楚這裡消失的點在哪裡 ; 一對夫妻在火星上 , 還有幾個在克雷蒙拉 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖馬利亞戴拉的皮亞扎克前面 , 在那裡 , 一場足球賽正在進行 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	現在這是一個被足球撞擊的可怕的插圖 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的碎片:那裡有聖母堂的步調 , 有足球 , 有一點鳥翅膀沒有發生 , 所以我必須重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想看聖馬利亞.迪拉的步調 , 這些書真的很有彈性 , 非常有互動性 , 只是把它轉過來 , 用另一種方式來看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到影響力在紅線中被捕捉 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥把自己拉過去 , 跨越了中世紀的大樓 , 僅有幾個中世紀的大樓 , 朝向聖塔教堂和周圍的圓頂 , 往下俯瞰我們已經提過、看過、看過、流過、流過了幾次 ; 還有bernis雕像 , 穿越了神奇的聖母堂 , 在26英尺高的直徑上 , 停止了足夠長的距離 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們可以在裡面和周圍 , 因為我們在飛行 , 在這個特定的時刻 , 我們不用擔心重力 , 所以這張圖可以在頁面上以任何方式呈現 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會感到有點高興 ; 這並不讓人訝異 , 以這種方式模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	穿過我剛剛談到的美好牆壁 , 佈滿了我所說的猶太人 ; 美麗的雕像裝進了新月上方的牆壁 , 上方是 " 崛起 " 的標誌等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後 , 我們到達了palazzo的庭院 , 也就是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓的一扇小窗口 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿上移除訊息 , 這是它說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看畫板時 , 我們看到他正在做的 , 事實上 , 一張鴿子剛剛拍攝的旅程的地圖 , 紅線延伸出所有的視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工的研究員skylartibbits在自我組裝上運作的想法 , 與其建造一些東西 , 我們可以創造出一股dnazips本身的方式 。 它是早期階段的一個大概念 ; tibbits向我們展示了三個自我組裝的計畫 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbits:我們能做出自己製造的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自行組合、複製和修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要給你們看我所相信的 , 是目前的製造業狀態 , 然後和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在目前的製造業狀態中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間--[組裝時間] , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜 , 全新的 , 令人興奮的科技在鋼筋、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年--[組裝時間]兩百五十萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒內折疊 , 或dna有三十億鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠比我們所能建造的任何東西都更有效率 , 遠比我們所能建造的任何東西更複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面的效率遠遠高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以為了長壽而修復自己
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 天然系統有個超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將它轉化為我們建造的環境 , 那麼我們就有一些令人興奮的潛力來建立東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中自組裝 , 我想有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 讓我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以用它來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能啟動的能量 , 讓我們的部件能夠從程式中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	而我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正冗長 , 來保證我們已經成功地建立了我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些計畫 , 是我和我在麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩個是巨型機器人和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些計畫是大規模可重組的機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們被嵌入機械電裝置、感應器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼你想要摺出來的東西 , 編成一系列的角度 , 如此負120 , 負120 , 0 , 120 , 負120 , 類似的120 , 類似的一系列角度 , 或轉彎 , 通過弦來傳送那序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都承受它的負面信息 , 轉到那 , 檢查是否到那裡 , 然後將它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 正在進行這個計畫 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 成千上萬美元 , 許多男人為了製作這個8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人嵌入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 並觀察被動的大自然 , 或被動地嘗試有重新配置的程式性 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它進一步更進一步 , 嘗試擁有實際的計算能力 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了計算最基本的建材 , 數位邏輯閘 , 直接進入你的零件 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是nandgate
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體是你計算的大門 , 你有兩個輸入四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 如同你在建造你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前一個被放置的磚塊
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後給你一個3d空間的輸出
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算了它之前所做的事和你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 往上或往下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於0輸出 , 就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是一個輸出值 , 它會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	所以真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們擁有所有被建構出來的信息 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱之為自體複製 , 因為你的結構包含了確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌入在內 , 告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有可以爬上去的東西 , 閱讀它 , 輸出一個到一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以我要展示的最後一個項目叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是目前最令人興奮的例子 , 被動自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要可重組性和可程式性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們都有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要轉右或左右 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以 , 當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上就是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該轉右或左右 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以 , 當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊成任何你編程的組合 , 所以在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體彼此相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以編寫任何立體的形狀或維度 , 二維的形狀完全被動地進入這個鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴了我們關於未來的什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我想 , 這告訴我們 , 有新的可能性可以自組裝、複製、修復 , 在我們的物理結構、建築、機器中 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分都有新的程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從中你可以有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚可以真正計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的平行和分散的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這很讓人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些計畫只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們實施這些新科技 , 為一個新的自我組裝的世界實現 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過海洋中最深的點兩次 。 下一代有什麼留給了什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家納森•沃爾菲提出了這個答案:幾乎一切 。 我們可以開始 , 帶著不可思議的小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃菲:要探索什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去拜訪威斯康辛州的貝洛伊 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡向一位偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews致敬
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯帶領了一系列的探險活動 , 到未經觸及的地區 , 例如在戈壁沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來他說 , 印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我在一群中學的學生上了一堂公開講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡要告訴各位 , 如果在ted這裡有比在ted演講更令人畏懼的話 , 它會試圖把一千個12歲的孩子的注意力放在一個45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一個問題真的困在我身上 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了一個問題: 「 我們應該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想 , 有一種感覺 , 我們很多人都擁有地球上探索的偉大時代已經結束了 , 對於下一代他們將必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到重要的探索事物 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	真的沒有什麼意義 , 可以讓我們在地球上探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起在生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這位探險家是馬丁尼烏斯•貝里克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck開始發現菸草鑲嵌病的成因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物取得受感染的汁液 , 他會透過更小的過濾器過濾過它 。
