and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了當時他覺得外面一定有些東西比當時所知最小型的生命形式還小
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀人命名 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 的病毒拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒的同時 , beijerinck真的為我們打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒組成了地球上絕大多數的基因信息 , 遠超過所有其他生命形式的基因信息組合 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然 , 已經有很大的實際應用 , 和這個世界有很大的關聯 , 比如天花消滅 , 疫苗對抗子宮頸癌 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類帕普洛馬病毒所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這可不是500年前的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	在一百多年前 , 北京人發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們卻沒意識到生命的形式 , 構成了地球上大部分的基因信息 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些了不起的工具 , 可以讓我們探索看不見的世界 , 像是深刻定序 , 讓我們能做得更多 , 不僅僅是從特定的物種中 , 觀察各個基因組 , 並且從各個特定物種中檢視完整的微生物群體 , 包括我們周遭的微生物群體 , 並且記錄這些物種中的所有基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧應用在土壤上 , 到皮膚上 , 以及兩者間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在在一個普通的基礎上做這件事 , 來找出造成它們的爆發造成的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓大家了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上抽取了一根娜絲 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常做的事 , 去尋找像流感病毒這種呼吸道病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究遺傳信息 , 我們會發現許多人的遺傳信息 , 當然 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大多來自你鼻子內完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常非常驚人的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始檢視這些資訊時 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡大約20%的遺傳信息並不符合我們從未見過的任何東西 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們沒有線索這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些研究這類數據的小組 , 我們當中少數人已經開始稱這些資訊為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的任何東西 , 它和我們遺傳信息中未知的大陸差不多 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是大量的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 其中的40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	甚至在相對保守的血液中 , 大約百分之一到二的信息是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法和我們以前看過的任何東西做配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們以為這就是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對是新的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越精確時 , 我們已經決定了這些資訊是一種生命的形式 , 至少有一些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設只有在它們的嬰兒時期 , 存在著非常令人興奮的可能性:在這個生命中埋藏著 , 在這個遺傳信息中 , 是尚未被辨識的生命的標誌 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	在我們探索a、t、c、g的這一串時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命階段 , 就像beijerinck一樣 , 會從根本上改變我們對生物的本質 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許會讓我們辨識出一種癌症的成因 , 會讓我們不熟悉或可能在分子生物學中創造出一種新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興能宣布 , 和史丹佛、加州理工和加州理工和加州理工學院的同事一起 , 我們目前正在開始一項倡議 , 探索生物暗物質 , 為新生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百多年前 , 人們沒意識到病毒 , 生命形式是構成我們星球上大部分基因信息的形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆我們可能完全沒有意識到我們鼻子底下的新生命 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經把地球上所有的大陸都收集起來 , 我們可能發現了外面所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的一課 , 讓來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們說出這堂課的話 , 會是這樣的:不要假設我們目前所認為的 , 是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	去過你選擇探索的領域的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們周圍有未知 , 他們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳說科學家daviddeutsch把理論物理放在後面的漢堡 , 來討論一個更迫切的問題:我們這個物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙、
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在我們在宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出一隻肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以 , 我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家已經知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一個 , 事實上 , 紀錄史上大部分人都知道的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 不論是什麼 , 都適合維持我們的進化或創造 , 就像以前的思想和我們現在的存在一樣 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這裡的想法是 , 在太空船外面 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 內部是我們所有的 , 我們都依賴的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 大家都已經知道的第二件事 , 和大多數人類歷史所相信的相反 , 人類並不是 , 事實上 , 存在的樞紐 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星軌道運行 , 位於典型銀河系的郊區 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道的兩件事 , 有點像是在說我們處在一個很不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合之類的 , 第二個是說我們正處於一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是 , 如果你把這兩個當作深刻的真理來生活 , 並且告訴你的生活決策 , 那麼它們似乎有點相互衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不會阻礙他們兩人完全虛假 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 所以 , 讓我從第二個開始 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們看看四周 , 看看隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 這完全不典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的只是朝著同一個方向走幾百英里 , 再回頭看 , 你完全看不到任何牆壁或化學污垢 , 你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你比那更進一步的話 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系、恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為恆星在星系中出現 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 都沒有任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們再往外走 , 直到我們在銀河系外面 , 回頭看 , 沒錯 , 那裡有巨大的銀河系 , 有著螺旋形的手臂在我們面前展現出來 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時我們已經從這裡走了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們還是沒有在宇宙中一個典型的地方附近 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須走一千倍 , 進入到星系間空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ?
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	在極大的花費下 , ted安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 呈現了星系間空間的觀點 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能讓燈光發光 , 拜託 , 這樣我們就能看見嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你可以看到 , 在星系間的星系間空間是完全黑暗的 , 暗暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	很黑的一點是 , 如果你要去看最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星被炸毀為超新星 , 你就要直接盯著它 , 當它的光接觸到你時 , 你仍然無法看見甚至閃耀 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙有多大和多麼黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的明亮 , 所以很聰明的一個事件 , 它會在幾光年內殺死你的石頭死去 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星系間空間來看 , 距離你甚至看不到 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面也非常寒冷 , 比絕對零度還低三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且是非常空虛的 。 真空的密度比目前地球上最好的科技所能創造的高一百萬倍 。 所以 , 一個典型的地方是如此不同 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	而這就是這個地方的典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何知道一個如此遙遠的環境 , 如此不同 , 與我們所習以為常的事物是如此的外星人 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球是我們的環境 , 以我們創造知識的形式 ,
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這意味著什麼 ? 嗯 , 比我們剛剛所說的還要更進一步 , 用望遠鏡 , 你會看到像恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們被稱為 「 quasars 」 。 quasars原本的意思是 「 量子主義物體 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	意思是看上去有點像恆星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 星系中心的物質就崩塌在超大質量的黑洞上 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了一些引力崩塌的能量 。 其中一些物質 , 回到巨大的噴射流中 , 以我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理學與噴射流的物理差不多 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法立即存活下來 。 語言在試圖描述其中一個噴射流中會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像體驗超新星爆炸 , 但在最遠的範圍內 , 一次數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那種噴射機在數十億年後就發生了一種方式 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 和模型 , 並且預測 , 並且解釋 , 在這幾十億年後發生的事 , 在現實中 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了一個精確的工作模型 , 其它的quasar 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅是它的超級完美圖像 , 雖然它也包含了它 , 但一個解釋性的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 對於一個結構的重組 , 就會隨著時間增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律具有這種特殊性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那種實體物體 , 和彼此不一樣 , 不論如何 , 都無法體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間 , 做得越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構含有 , 含有不斷增加的精確度 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 和宇宙中的其他地方 , 都包含在自己內部的結構和因果本質上 。 所以 , 遠離不足的物理定律 , 物理定律允許這一切發生 , 甚至命令這一切 , 是物理學最重要的事之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們和宇宙其他地方的形式 , 如何取得這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	關於史蒂芬霍金的論點 , 有一件事是真的 , 我的意思是 , 它是真的 , 但它是錯誤的強調 。 有一件事是真的 , 它沒有任何特殊的物理 。 沒有特殊的解藥 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它只用我們在豐富中所擁有的三樣東西來做 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 完全沒有物質的製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體成效 , 來記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放式知識、解釋的開放創造來說 , 很重要的就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好可以去做測試 , 比如 , 牛頓的引力定律大約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們過去的證據卻在地球的每平方米上落了數十億年 , 之後會持續數十億年 。 其他的科學也是一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 只是為了我們星球上發生的 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點飽和了證據 , 同時也伴隨著物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三項知識開放創造的前提條件 , 是他們最低的可能供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 它是空的 , 它是冷的 , 外面是暗的 , 還是暗的 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實 , 那只是另一種類型的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像在星系間空間中有一個立方體 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 立方體對人類的標準是非常空虛的 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造出自身的太空站 , 在那裡 , 有一群科學家致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 它已經超越了現有的技術 , 甚至將來自星系間空間的氫氣收集起來 , 將之變成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼可能阻礙我們去做 , 除了知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們可以自動取得能源供應 , 因為變異會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 這對人類的感官來說是黑暗的 。 但你只需要拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是當天設計的其中一個 , 向外看 , 你會看到我們從這裡看到的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	用一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將可以看見恆星 , 和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將可以做到天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	當地你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最困難的科學可能是生物學領域之旅 , 因為要花數億年才能到達最近的生命之星 , 再回來 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴你們 , 對不起 , 理查 , 但我從來不喜歡生物學領域的旅行 , 我想我們每隔幾億年就能做到一千萬年 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了所有開放式知識的先例 。 任何這樣一個立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何一個角落 , 都可能變成我們一樣的樞紐 , 如果我們知道如何做這些事情的知識 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不在獨特的居住地
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間有能力創造出一個開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都一樣 。 這是地球 。 這是一個被污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在這裡 , 並不是資源 , 因為資源充足 , 而是知識 , 也就是稀少的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個以宇宙為基礎的觀點 , 或許我認為應該要讓我們覺得非常特別 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有具體的知識存在於宇宙中持續的挑戰 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超新星在幾光年之外就熄滅 , 我們都會死 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	martinrees最近寫了一本關於我們脆弱的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出了差錯 , 最重要的是要用大規模毀滅性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	而他認為文明在這個世紀只有50%的機率存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他稍後會談到這點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為機率是正確的類別來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但是我對他有所認同 。 我們可以生存 , 我們也無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機會 , 而是我們是否在時間上創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並非前所未有的 。 物種隨時都滅絕了 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明結束了 。 絕大多數的物種和所有曾經存在過的文明現在都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼 , 我們唯一的希望就是利用一個特徵 , 區別我們物種 , 和我們文明的特徵 , 從其他所有人的角度來看 , 我們和物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋能力 , 新的知識成為存在的樞紐 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 現在讓我把這個應用在當前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 只是為了說明我所說的那種 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 。 不管是全球暖化 , 我只是一個layman 。 而layman的理性是認真看待預防科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果這是真的 , 我們當下最好的選項就是防止二氧化碳的排放 , 像是京都議定書 , 在經濟活動上的限制 , 以及它的巨額成本上千億美元或不論它是什麼 , 那就已經是任何合理的措施造成的災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而被擁護的行動 , 甚至不被驅逐去解決問題 , 只不過是輕而易舉而已 。 所以已經太晚才避免它 , 可能已經太晚了 , 以至於任何人都意識到危機之前 , 都已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代 , 可能已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論在告訴我們 , 工業排放即將達到一個新的冰河時期 , 數十億人會死去 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一教訓對我來說似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們無法永遠知道 。 當我們知道一個令人不安的災難時 , 以及如何用比災難本身的成本來解決它 , 那麼就不會有太多的爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們還沒有預防的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要有問題的立場 , 而不僅是問題的解決方案 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	真的 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的療法 , 但只有當我們知道該預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你已經被打到鼻子上了 , 那麼醫學的科學並不符合教導你如何避免打孔 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫療科學停止尋求解藥 , 只專注在預防上 , 那它也會達到非常少的成就 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	此刻世界正在震驚 , 計畫在氣體排放的同時 , 完全不需要成本來降低氣體排放 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要和計畫相處 , 以降低溫度 , 和計畫要在更高的溫度下生活 , 而不是全部的成本 , 而是有效率且便宜的 。 還有一些這樣的計畫存在 , 像是在太空中一群鏡子 , 來將陽光反射出來 , 並鼓勵水產生物吃進更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	在當下 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力去面對這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 正確的能力不是避免無限期的好運 , 我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩張石板 , 刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個 , 卡維: 「 問題是解決的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	而另一張地毯上: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家要如何脫離貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不好的規則系統中 ? 經濟學家paulromer揭露了一個大膽的想法: 「 憲章城市 」 , 城市規模管理區是由國家聯盟所統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的激進想法:charter城市
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	這對我們來說是非常吸引人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在街燈下做功課 , 在資本城市的機場裡 , 因為他們家沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	現在 , 我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫裡的那件
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們給他一個名字 , 尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭尼爾森有一支手機 ,
so here is the puzzle .	這個謎題是:
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森能取得尖端科技 , 比如手機 , 但無法取得100歲的科技 , 用來在家裡發電燈嗎 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	現在 , 以一個字來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防那種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們可以把新科技帶進去 , 讓他們能接觸到像納爾森這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一條規則下運作 , 它說 , 它必須以非常低、補貼的價格在每單位售出的價格下賣出的電力 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它沒有資源 , 也沒有獎勵 , 沒有其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想改變這個規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他被看見 , 有可能有不同的規則 , 規定企業賺取小額的利潤 , 所以他們有誘因去簽署更多顧客 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	也就是手機公司所採購的那種規則 , 尼爾森從下面運作的電話中採購他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經看過這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變對電力施用的規則 , 但卻碰到來自企業和消費者的抗議 , 他們想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他卡在規則上 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	而尼爾森被卡在街燈下研究 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	接下來真正的挑戰是試著找出我們如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有些規則是我們能發展出改變規則的 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想主張 , 有一個廣義抽象的洞見 , 我們可以做出實用的 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多的選擇 , 而更多選擇的領導者 , 在許多國家中 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現這兩者之間的反對意見是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你想給予領導者的那種選擇 , 像是給總統機會提高電價的選擇 , 帶走經濟體中人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇能夠繼續消費補貼電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一方或另一方 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到能給予兩者更多選擇的方法 , 那就能給我們一套改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , 尼爾森也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的損害效應 , 規則能讓人們保持在黑暗中 , 看看太空總署在夜晚從地球上拍到的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是在亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大來看 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在線上 , 這就像一個黑洞 , 和它的鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們在黑暗中保持在那裡 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但重要的是要體認到北韓和南韓 , 起源於法律和規定的一套相同的規則 , 同時也在更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致了非常多樣化的路徑給他們的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	因此 , 我們可以改變身為人類的我們 , 可以改變我們用來和彼此互動的規則 , 更好、更壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 在這裡線上 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗 , 相較於它的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 這裡有著相同數量的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相較於波多黎各 , 其居民有一半是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規定是不好的 , 因為政府是弱勢 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則不好 , 因為政府太堅強和壓迫了 , 如同北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想創造出有好規則的環境 , 我們就不能直接撕掉 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得找到方法來建立 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大幅展現出與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的開始 , 中國是世界高科技領導者 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅的技術 , 如鋼、印刷、槍械等 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 來鼓勵那些想法的傳播 , 一個能促進傳播的利潤動機 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 減緩了創新 , 把中國從世界其他地方砍掉 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 如同世界上其他國家創新的同時 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 也發展了新的規則 , 中國人從那些進步中被砍掉了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	在那裡的收入停滯不前 , 隨著它在世界其他地方的領先放大 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	接下來這張圖表比較近期的數據
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了收入 , 中國的平均收入為美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到大約百分之三的百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代後期 , 有些事情改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	在中國開始成長 。 中國人很快就趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回到地圖上 , 你可以得到一個線索 , 來引起中國規則的戲劇性改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地點 , 在這裡你可以看到的線的邊緣 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的中國 , 以非常不同的規則運作 , 比起其它主導的大陸中國規則 , 這些規則來自當時的勞動市場經濟 , 並且由英國政府主導 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 開始工作 , 像是縫製衣服 , 製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了取得增加收入的過程 , 越來越多的技能導致快速成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典範 , 像鄧小平這樣的領導人可以複製 , 當他們決定將所有的主島移向市場模式 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地明白了對他人民提供選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫每個在中國的人 , 立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們通過創造一些特殊的區塊 , 在某種意義上 , 英國所做的 , 讓這個機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要選項的人能有機會選擇 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以 , 他們在香港周圍創立了四個特別的經濟區:中國可以來上班的區塊 , 城市在很快的地方長大 ; 還有外國公司可以進來 , 製造東西的區塊 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有一個叫做深圳的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡有一間台灣公司 , 讓你們很多人有的iphone , 他們用中國人的勞工搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有十四個沿岸風箏在同一個意義上開放 , 最後在這些地方展示成功 , 人們可以選擇選擇 , 因爲他們所提供的優勢被關起來 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡的成功 , 導致了一項共識 , 朝向整個經濟體的市場模式前進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子顯示了幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	一是:為人們保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	二:在適當的尺度上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落裡的規則 , 你可以這樣做 , 但村落會太小 , 以免有數百萬人在良好的規則下能得到你所能得到的好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你不能給某些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果 , 然後讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你這個機會 , 創造新地方 , 有新的規則 , 人們可以選擇要去做 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	他們大到可以得到所有好處當我們數百萬人在良好的規則下一起工作
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是 , 我們對於所謂的 「 特許城市 」 的概念 ,
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定的憲章開始 , 專門吸引建造城市的人所需的所有規則 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立基礎設施──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 他們會先雇用那些搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你會需要吸引家人 , 那些會來到那裡的居民 , 永久生活 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這份憲章 , 人們會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建立起來 。
and we can scale this model .	而我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍的
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中捕捉到的
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	那真的是建立在模型上 , 如果我們能在未居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的憲章底下生活 , 但沒有人被迫生活在其中 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是對領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的領導者們的選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作關係有潛力:國家合作的案例 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先是市場模式的小規模 , 然後擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意的 , 透過它在香港的行動 , 比上世紀所有援助計畫都還要更能減少世界貧窮 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這類的夥伴再複製這一類的夥伴 , 我們就能讓這類的利益擴散到世界各地 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到負責任的授權 , 一個從一個國家到另一個國家的授權 , 來接管某種行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說時 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 。 但重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時會出現的那種情緒 , 可以順便提一下 , 可以讓我們再拉回來 , 可以讓我們關閉我們的能力 , 我們對探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	關於殖民主義的壞處在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 所謂的壞處在於它涉及了強制和認知的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式全是關於選擇 , 無論是領導者 , 還是那些會住在這些新地方的人們 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而 , 選擇是對強迫和認知的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談這要如何在實踐中扮演 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	以一位特定的領袖raulcastro為例 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定發生過 , 他有機會為古巴做的事 , 為中國做了什麼 , 但他在古巴島上沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 南部有一點點光 , 南邊有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一個區域 , 位於關塔那摩灣 , 在那裡 , 一個條約給了美國政府負責的一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚到加拿大總理說: 「 聽好 , 伊安克斯有個可怕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要脫身 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 接管 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特殊的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新的城市在上面建設 。
allow many people to come in .	允許許多人進來
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓附近的香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那座城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會拿回來 。 但這將會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結到我的國家的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還在哪裡呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	當中許多人完全得到人們可以選擇的特殊區塊的概念 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人們不受強迫的意見 , 和強迫可以強迫的反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更可靠的承諾 , 那些投資者會來建造港口、建造道路 , 在新城市中 , 他們可以做出更可靠的承諾 , 如果他們和夥伴國家合作 , 就能做出更可靠的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許 , 甚至在某些安排有點像escrow帳號 , 你把土地放在escrow帳號中 , 合夥的國家負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多土地 , 新城市可以建設 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	有巨大的土地像這片土地 , 數億人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們歸納一下 , 想想看 , 不僅僅是一兩個章節 , 還會有數十個城市 , 能協助創造出數億個城市 , 也許未來數十億人口會移居到城市中 , 那裡有足夠的土地供給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們晚上看著燈光 , 誤導的一件事是 , 視覺上看來 , 大部分的世界已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我來展示一下為什麼會這樣是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這所有土地的代表為例
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它轉變成一個方塊 , 代表著地球上所有可耕地的土地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被30億人口居住的城市所佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 現有30億城市居民的城市只佔了地球上3%的可耕地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們會像這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從百分之三的耕地 , 降到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大降低地球上人類的足跡 , 做法是建造更多人們可以搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被好的規則治理 , 城市可以是人們安全免於犯罪、安全疾病和壞的衛生設施的城市 , 人們有機會得到一份工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到像電一樣的基本用途 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座特定城市 , 要怎麼樣才能建造出更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它有助於使用手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的 , 就是寫一些細節 , 可能進到這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們經營城市 , 出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外出去 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 比如 , 假設它不僅是加拿大 , 和拉爾•卡斯楚的交易 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 西班牙也是 。 也許古巴想要成為四面向關節創投的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	對此還沒那麼先例 , 但那很容易就成功了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這個 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港是新加坡和香港的城市 , 使得他們開始時所擁有的土地價值大大增加 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值來支付像是警察、法庭 , 但學校體制和健康照護體制 , 這使得土地更有吸引力 , 使得人們有更高的收入 , 順便說 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 人們幫忙建設這個區塊的動機 , 並設立基本規則 , 走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多其他的細節 , 像這樣 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們怎麼可能有低成本又負擔得起的建築物在第一份工作中 , 組裝像iphone一樣的東西 , 但讓那些建築物能有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會在地震或颶風中落下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節要解決 , 但已經開始追求這些事情的人已經知道沒有路障 , 沒有障礙 , 除了想像中的失敗之外 , 還會讓我們無法在真正的全球雙贏解決方案上實現 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來做個結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此好地擺脫 , 即使地球上有太多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像稀有物品 , 分享的意思是 , 我們每人得到的都比較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那樣的方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會考慮科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另外一類的想法:管理我們如何彼此互動的規則 ; 規則如 , 讓稅法系統支持一項研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有個系統 , 我們有土地的所有權 , 在政府辦公室裡註冊 , 讓人們可以當殖民地 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們規則的空間 , 尤其是想出改變規則的規則 , 這樣我們就不會陷入不好的規則 , 那麼我們就能繼續向前進 , 真正讓世界變得更美好 , 讓像納爾遜和他的朋友不需要在街燈下研究 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先鋒克萊格•凡特從史詩般的圓形探險中休息 , 來談他的團隊目前為止發現了數百萬個基因 , 用來描繪海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生態圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技等 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna上的craigventer和海底的craigventer
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對衰老辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這將是我唯一對它的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我明白樂觀主義者絕對過於悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我十八分鐘內要告訴各位的是 , 我們要如何從閱讀基因密碼轉換到開始自己寫程式的第一步 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在十年前 , 當我們發表了第一個免費生命體的序列 , 那個流感流行的大象 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這項計畫從13年降到4個月後 ,
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在2到8個小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去的十年中 , 大量的基因組被加入了:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳動物 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前 , 思想的基因組學是在今年底 , 我們可能有三到五組基因組定序 ; 它是幾百組的順序 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	今年我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金會取得了一項補助金 , 作為環保有機體的副程式 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因編碼的比率已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有把表面刮到這個星球的可得性 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人都沒有意識到 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成的大約是地球生物量的一半 , 而所有的動物都只組成了所有生物量的一分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不常做的事 , 但如果你有機會到海裡去 , 然後吞下一口海水 , 請記住每毫升有大約一百萬個細菌 , 以及一千萬個病毒的順序 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到五千種微生物物種在兩年前就被特徵化了所以我們決定要做點什麼
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們成立了srcer第二次遠征 , 和偉大的海洋學探險一樣 , 每200英里就嘗試採樣海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始進行測試計畫 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越加拉巴哥群島 , 然後穿越太平洋 , 我們現在在整個印度洋的路上工作 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的職責 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有部分是要協助讓年輕人對進入科學的興奮 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只要把海水過濾過 , 然後在不同的濾鏡上蒐集不同大小的生物體 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時就能完成一億個基因編碼的序列 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這樣做 , 我們做出了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉個例子 , 被認為眼睛裡的視覺顏料只有一個或兩個有機體在環境中有相同的顏料
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎世界上溫暖地區的海底上層的每一個物種都有相同的光受體 , 並將陽光當作它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因 , 和五萬種新種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經把這個延伸到空氣中 , 帶著來自斯隆基金會的一個補助金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 我們所有人每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上或關閉聽器 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的器具過濾過 ; 我們收集到十億微生物的順序 , 僅僅一天 , 在紐約市的一棟建築物上面過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	目前我們正處於定序的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在數據收集的一面 , 就在我們穿過加拉巴哥群島的地方 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每200英里 , 我們會在海洋中的樣本中看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合乎邏輯的 , 以不同溫度的梯度來說 ,
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	所以 , 這是一張衛星照片 , 根據溫度紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現 , 溫水樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差別 , 就豐富的物種而言 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一個讓我們相當驚訝的是 , 這些光受體會偵測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些轉型極大的從地區到地區 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海裡 , 大部分是藍色的地方 , 光感受體往看藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有很多葉綠素在周圍時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們更有不同 , 可能在極端的情況下 , 朝紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	只是為了評估我們的基因修補法 , 我們把所有資料組合起來 , 包括遠離探險的所有資料 , 這代表地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 且它總共大約有2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放入基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們是否只是發現了已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但是我們在環境中的每一個新樣本 , 都以線性的方式加入這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們在這個星球上最早的發現階段 , 關於基本基因、成分和生命 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的進化樹 , 我們在右上角和動物在一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約2900萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組中只有24 , 000個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物集合在一起 , 我們可能共有不到三萬種 , 也許十幾千種不同的基因家族 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因現在不僅是進化的設計成分 ,
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 以基因為中心的觀點回到理查德•道金斯的想法 , 比起以基因為中心的觀點 , 這些基因組件的構造不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年或兩年間 , 都已經改變了 , dna定序的速度很快 , 且很便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們第一次想到合成基因組學在1995年的第二組基因組定序後 , 出現了這個基因組 , 也是從菌絲體生殖器上得到的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們簡單地問了一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800個 , 另一個500個 , 是否有一組較小的基因組成一個最小的操作系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做變性突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉錄器只是小片段的dna , 在基因編碼中隨機插入 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們插入基因中間 , 它們就會瓦解它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖上的所有基因 , 可以拿走轉錄器插入 , 我們稱之為 「 不必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能根據環境中的東西來定義一個必要或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著採用更直接的智能方法 , 用13種相關的有機體的基因組 , 我們試著比較所有這些 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現只有173個基因共有 , 共有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	池塘擴張一點 , 如果我們忽略了一種細胞寄生蟲 ; 它擴張的更大 , 大約在310左右時 , 核心基因組成 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴大或收縮基因組 , 取決於你在這裡的觀點 , 到大約300到400個基因 , 來自500的最小 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法就是用這些基因來建構人工染色體 , 我們必須用以casette為基礎的時尚來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片中合成正確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 我的同事們 , 開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能夠合成一個五千個鹼基對的病毒 , 只有一個兩週的時間 , 即百分之百準確度 , 以它的序列和它的生物學來說 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個相當令人興奮的實驗當我們把合成的dna注入細菌中突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產然後轉身殺死細菌
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一批合成病毒--小兒麻痺症病毒在一年前就已經製造過一年 , 但它的活性只有十分之一 , 花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構的漫畫
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個案例是軟體現在建立自己的硬體 , 那就是我們有生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上跳到關心生物戰場我最近在參議院委員會前的證詞美國政府設立了一個特別的委員會來審查這個地區
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實保持在心中 , 與人們的想像是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何今天已經被定序的病毒 , 基因組可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會對伊波拉或天花的事物感到害怕 , 但這種有機體的dna並不具有感染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關心安全部門擁有的 , 是設計家病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 主要努力試圖創造生物戰務經紀人 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那個研究真正不連續的話 , 未來應該要有非常少的活動來製造設計師病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內就有可能
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	而可能是uk類細胞 , 我們所擁有的這些細胞 , 在十年內就有可能實現 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在製造數十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以將這些種姓和基因轉換成人造染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 要怎麼把所有其他人都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個全然的組合系統 , 將這些組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體、deinococcusradiodurans衍生出來的 , 可以承受三百萬雷達的輻射 , 而不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在這個輻射爆炸之後 , 它重新組合了它的基因組 , 大約12到24小時 , 在它的染色體被拆開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能存在於外太空 , 因為我們在那裡旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是五十萬雷達輻射後的一個玻璃beaker 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和破裂 , 微生物坐在海底 , 變得更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡是一張實際的圖片:這張圖片的上方顯示了一百七十萬rad輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體是真的分崩離析 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	在這裡 , 同樣的dna會在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物能做到這一點 , 我們可能有成千上萬的 , 如果不在這星球上 , 有能力做到這一點的不同物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成之後 , 第一步只是移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 也為了希望環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們排序的第三個有機體 , 甲烷藻類--jannacus--它生活在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 而它所有的碳都來自於它從環境中捕捉回來的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 成千上萬種不同的生物 , 存活於二氧化碳之外 , 還可以捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其使用從石油取得合成過程的碳 , 我們有機會從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物 , 活於碳一氧化碳中 , 我們用它作為降低能量 , 將水分解 , 產生氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有數條路徑 , 可以被工程代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一個重大的方案 , 和挪威的石油合作 , 來捕捉並將甲烷從那裡轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短時間內 , 我認為會有一個新的領域叫做 「 組合基因體 」 , 因為有這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列和同質組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天製造出大約一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學一樣 , 你通過篩選 , 不論你是在篩選氫產物 , 還是化學產物 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 會在到達內部 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光下產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們有氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合細胞 , 分解複雜糖分解的酵素 , 變成簡單的糖和發酵方式 , 在同一個細胞中製造乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥品生產已經在主要實驗室裡使用微生物
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學成份 , 比我們最好的化學家能產生的複雜度還要多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境救援的來源 , 以及也許取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來結束演講 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們延遲了1999年的實驗開始 , 直到我們完成一年半的生物倫理審查 , 到我們是否應該嘗試做人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都用他們的文字作為法律書籍 , 他們無法在他們身上找到任何東西 , 禁止製造生命 , 所以一定是沒關係的 。 唯一的關注是生物戰的一個面向 , 但給了我們前面這些實驗是為了我們做這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在的斯隆基金會剛剛資助了一項關於這方面的機構研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和益處 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 如我自己應該在這個領域使用的規則 , 我們正努力設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們很簡單的議題在於 , 我們能否設計東西來生產乾淨能源 , 也許革命開發中國家能做些什麼 , 並透過各種簡單的過程提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•津巴多說快樂和成功根源於我們大多數人都不認同:我們向過去、現在和未來邁進 。 他建議我們在時間上校正我們的生活的第一步 , 改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理學、科學
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了一份健康的處方 , 花在時間上 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些點子 , 關於時間的秘密 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘 。 30秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安定下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	而是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們來談談亞當的誘惑 , 校長的對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來到亞當 , 別這麼想洗衣服 , 咬一口 。 」 「 我真的有 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口咬 , 亞當 , 不要放棄夏娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 。 一口咬了 。 到底是什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘人的 。 一切都是為了產生、抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 之後 , 衝動 , 反思 , 焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	保證美德會落入當下的熱情中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的女孩 , 主導了性不識字和處女 , 直到婚姻──謝謝布希──大多數 , 60%──在一年內 , 產出性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都沒有使用節育器 。
so much for promises .	對承諾這麼多 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓四歲小孩誘惑 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖了 。 但如果他們等到實驗人員回來 , 他們可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然要付出代價 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 現在延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 14年後回去 , 試圖發現那些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在很多方面 , 都有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抵制坐姿的孩子們高出250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很巨大 。 那就像一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有陷入多大的麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且決心的 。 今天對我來說 , 關鍵是 , 他們是未來的焦點 , 而不是呈現出來 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 把你人的經驗分成時間區塊或時間類別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動、無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化、國家之間、個人之間、社會階級、教育程度之間有所不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們可以變得偏頗 , 因為你學會把其中的一些消耗掉 , 並且利用其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	什麼決定了你做的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 來決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在立即的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你在感受什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們在那個格式中做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 呈現 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的樣子 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是無關緊要的
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱這些人為 「 牧師 」 , 因為他們關注的是
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在 , 只和未來有關 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是要預期後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們會稱他們為 「 未來式 」 。 他們的焦點在於將來會是什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要爭論 , 時間觀點的悖論 , 會影響你做出的每一個決定 , 你完全沒有意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	以上是你有偏見的時間觀點的程度 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以呈現 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被放大 , 兩種方式可以當作未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	可以把焦點放在正面的 , 或過度負面的
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是無私的 , 即你把焦點放在人生的喜悅上 , 或說是虛假主義者--這無關緊要 , 你的生活被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:即 , 生命始於死後 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展心理靈活性 , 將時間觀點轉移到流動 , 取決於情況的需求 , 這才是你要學的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度過於正面的 , 高度依賴未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和現代化的流動性 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和虛假主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的暫時性混合體就是你從過去的觀念中所得到的 , 給你根 。 你將你的家人、身份和自我連結起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的就是翅膀去翱翔 , 到新的目的 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的 「 享樂主義 」 得到的 , 是探索自己、地方、人、感知的能量 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	過剩的任何時間觀點都比正面更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來對成功的犧牲是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	犧牲家庭時間、犧牲朋友時間、
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲了好玩的時間 , 犧牲了個人的成人 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 , 犧牲了睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	而他們為工作、成就和控制而活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定 , 和一些ted成員共鳴
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我產生了共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯貧民區長大 , 一個西西里亞家庭 , 每個人都生活在過去和現在 。
