i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我身為一個未來的身份 , 走過頂端的人 , 做這些犧牲 , 因為老師們介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你會得到兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了簡報 , 我把焦點放在過去的觀念上 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用在許多世界的問題上:改變學校的輟學率 , 結合成癮 , 增強青少年的健康 , 用時間隱喻來治癒風險 , 讓奇蹟能促進永續和保育 , 降低身體復健率 , 改變自殺式恐怖分子的訴求 , 改變家庭間的衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是:許多生命的謎題可以藉由了解你的時間觀點和他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	今天有多少頭條會在一百年後重要 ? 一百年 ? 凱特朗的《長新聞》專案收藏了不只重要的故事 , 還會產生數十年來的共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調最近的頭條標題 , 有潛力塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的新聞
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞中淹沒 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是透明者一年就放出三百五十萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在長期來看 , 這些故事有多少會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是由現在的長期基金會成立的 , 是由tedsters所成立的 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華特•布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們在尋找的新聞可能仍然是50或100 , 000年後的新聞 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你看新聞通過過濾器時 , 很多東西都掉下來了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 為了從a.p.上方的故事 , 會不會在十年後才有意義 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	50或100年後這會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年最頂尖的故事是經濟 , 我打賭 , 不久後 , 這種特別的衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 對未來來說 , 什麼樣的故事可能會造成改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會透過我們的血液修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠的話 , 那天已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近一些故事:奈米蜂帶有真正的蜜蜂毒液的腫瘤 ; 它們將基因送入大腦 ; 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在有60億人的餵養困難 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如昨天我們聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國人會在沒有基因改造作物的情況下挨餓 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	比爾•蓋茲 , 很幸運地 , 已經賭上十億在[掌控]研究上 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會變得很不一樣 , 如果中國設定了議程 , 他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經過度把美國當作世界最大的汽車市場 , 他們過度把德國當作最大的出口者 , 他們開始在孩子身上做dna檢測 , 以選擇他們的事業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們找到各種方法來推回我們所知道的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:從阿根廷有一個蟻群現在已經散播到每個大陸但南極洲 ; 有一位自主的機器人科學家 , 很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命可能已經不需要我們了 ; 一個經過十二萬年後 , 才會醒來的微生物 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 沒有了我們 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但去年 , 我選了一長期新聞報導的主題是:月球上的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓它更容易放到上面的蟻群 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果太空總署不做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某人可能會寫大檢查 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長期來看 , 有些新聞報導比其他人更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡洛琳•波科展現了卡西尼航行到土星的影像 , 把焦點放在它最大的衛星泰坦 , 和凍土衛二上 , 似乎會射出冰的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、空間、科技、視覺化、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco飛到土星上 ,
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的十八分鐘裡 , 我將帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這趟旅程 , 你我已經走了很多年了 , 它從50年前開始 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不僅僅在月球上 , 還在月球上設置了飛行器 , 我們已經把機械太空船載載到所有行星上 , 我們已經登陸了小行星 , 和彗星結合在一起 , 在此時 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 飛到冥王星上 , 前人稱之為行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	而所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程中更大的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解某件事 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球 , 而我們 , 活在它之上 , 來了 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中 , 所有我們可能去的地方 , 尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 都有土星 。 我們在1980年代初期去過土星 , 但我們對土星的調查 , 自從卡西尼號太空船飛行了七年以來 , 在2004年的夏天時期 , 到處繞著土星運行 , 成為了人類最遙遠的機械裝置 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是一個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 以及顯然超越了比對 , 這個系統的調查達到巨大的宇宙 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究環狀物 , 我們就要學到很多關於恆星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張美麗的圖片是andromedanebula , 它是我們最接近、最大的螺旋星系到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	然後 , 這裡有個美麗的旋風星系的組合物由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程 , 也是人類航行的一個比喻 , 來了解我們周遭所有事物的相互連結 , 以及人類如何符合這張圖片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們和卡西尼所學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看我們過去兩年半拍攝的所有美麗照片 , 因為我就是沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我要集中在兩個最令人興奮的故事中 , 那些故事從這個重大的探索探險中浮現出來 , 我們在土星周圍進行 , 已經有兩年半了 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星被非常大且多樣化的月球收集所包含 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們從幾公里大小到跟美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝的大部份美麗的圖片事實上 , 土星和一些月亮相符 。 這裡是土星和土星 , 然後 , 土星展示了環形的邊緣 , 展示出它們有多稀薄 , 和月球土衛二相連 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星的四十七個衛星中有兩個是站立的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	而那些是泰坦和土衛六 。 泰坦是土星最大的月亮 , 直到卡西尼號到達那裡 , 是我們太陽系中最大的未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這種身體長久以來都在觀察行星的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境比較像是我們在地球上所存在的環境 , 或至少過去的太陽系中任何其他的身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是分子氮 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸一樣 , 只不過它的大氣含有簡單的有機物質 , 比如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在土衛六大氣層中高度會被破壞 , 而它們的產品會加入 , 來製造出hazeles 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個結局無所不在 , 完全是全球化和隱藏土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你不能用我們的眼睛看待表面 , 在光譜上的可見區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些haze粒子 , 被取笑了 , 在我們到達卡西尼號之前 , 經過數十億年和數十億年 , 溫和地下到地表上 , 將地表覆蓋在厚厚的有機水層中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以 , 像泰坦等同於焦油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們所懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以在土衛六的表面溫度下成為液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是要霸佔地球的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣層中是可以凝聚的 , 因此認知到這個情況 , 帶到前面一個奇異的可能性世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在這些雲朵之上 , 你有這幾百公里的haze , 防止任何陽光到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是華氏零度以下的350度
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但 , 儘管如此寒冷 , 你還是可能有雨落在土衛六的表面 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上下雨的做法是:它會雕刻天花板 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它可以創造峽谷 ; 它可以在大盆地和隕石坑中裝水 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把雪橇洗掉高山高峰 , 下到低地 , 停下來想一會 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像泰坦的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它很暗 。 土衛六的高中午和地球上深處一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很不錯 , 可能是下雨 , 你可能站在密西根湖的邊緣 , 用油漆薄薄荷 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	在我們和卡西尼號一起到達之前 , 我們有土衛六表面的觀點 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上所發現的 , 雖然它在細節上並不相同 , 和那個故事一樣迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼族人 , 曾是弗內斯•凡恩的冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有厚、延伸的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 太陽的背光 , 帶著光環作為一個美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月亮 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是非常大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器 , 可以透過這個大氣層看到水面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你看到的是明亮又暗的區域 , 這跟我們得到的差不多 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在是太神秘了:我們無法搞清楚我們在土衛六上所看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你更仔細看這個區域 , 你會開始看到像我們不認識的無線通道 。 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 我們後來發現 , 其實是一個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面上只有極少的隕石坑 , 意思是 , 它是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	而有些特徵看起來像板塊 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像已經被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在星球上看到任何線性 , 就表示有像斷層一樣的斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經在地表上改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但是我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一個事件發生在卡西尼號調查泰坦的高光下 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	而那是huygens探測器的部署 , 歐洲的huygens探測器──卡西尼在太陽系整整七年 。 我們把它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了2.5小時才能下降 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調一個事件有多重大 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它降落在外太陽系 , 這是人類史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	非常顯著 , 在我心中 , 這個事件應該要被美國和歐洲各個城市的膠帶帶帶帶帶帶帶遊行慶祝 。 可悲的是 , 那不是這樣 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因的顯著意義 。 這是個國際任務 , 這個事件在歐洲、在德國、在慶祝報告中被賦予英語口音、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利語 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這場示威展示了 「 聯合國 」 這個詞的意義:一個真正的聯合國團結在一起 , 為好的努力而努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要探索一個星球 , 要了解一個行星系統 , 對人類歷史而言 , 它是不可或缺的 , 而現在人類已經碰觸到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我剛剛談到雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極度情緒化的事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記的事 , 你也不該如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但無論如何 , 探測器在下方的路上採取了大氣的測量值 , 同時也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴你們看第一張來自探測器的土衛六表面的照片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這是個驚人之舉 , 因為那是所有我們想要的照片 , 從軌道上拍到的 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是一種不確定的模式 , 一種地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	一種只靠液體流動才能形成的趨勢 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些管道 , 看看它們是如何匯合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們匯聚到這裡 , 流入這個區域的管道 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里時拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在八公里長拍的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 十六公里 , 八公里--這大約是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫越美國 , 你就要飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	所以 , 這是你在泰坦飛機的窗口所拍攝的照片 , 橫跨土衛六的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器來到地表上休息 , 我將展示給你們看 , 各位先生女士 , 第一張從外太陽系表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水的冰泡 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在了其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們落入的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器基本上是土衛六等於一片泥土平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一片未解析過的地面 , 含有液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這樣 , 這種材料已經從土衛六的高地上沖下來 , 透過我們看到的這些通道 , 經過數十億年的排水 , 來填滿低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器登陸的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然 , 在我們的影像中沒有標誌 , 甚至在惠更斯的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 在我們找到沙丘時 , 它變得更令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六的赤道地區的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是一百公尺高 , 被幾公里的距離隔開 , 走了幾英里、幾英里、幾英哩 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有幾百個 , 高達一千或一千兩百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的薩哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 它讓人驚訝的是 , 沒有液體 , 直到最後 , 我們在極地區域看到湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	泰坦南極地區有個湖泊的景象 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	跟安大略湖差不多大
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 僅僅一個半星期前 , 我們飛越了泰坦北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了一個和卡斯皮亞海一樣大的特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節 , 顯然是在泰坦的極點 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們發現泰坦是個很了不起、神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 它是外星人 , 但卻是奇怪的地球形態 , 擁有地球形態和地理多樣性 , 且它是一個非常迷人的世界 , 太陽系中只有對地球本身的複雜性和豐富性 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們到了土衛二 。 土衛二是個小衛星 , 大約是泰坦的十分之一大 。 你可以看到它在英格蘭旁邊 , 只是為了展示它 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 非常明亮 , 它的表面顯然是用裂痕來折斷 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的媽媽在南極發現 , 我們看到的是南極的發現 , 我們發現了破裂的這個系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	而它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被編碼 。 這些碎片被有機材料所包裹 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整體 , 整個區域 , 南極區域已經升溫了 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就跟發現地球上的南極洲比熱帶地區還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍了額外的照片時 , 我們發現從這些碎片中 , 正是噴射出微小的冰粒 , 將數百英里延伸到太空中 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	而當我們把這張圖片編碼出來時 , 我們會看到這些噴射流進土衛二上千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊有類似的影像 , 像這張 , 思考過來自卡西尼號的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射流可能是從土衛二表面下的液態水中噴發出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能是液態水、有機物質和過多的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或換句話說 , 一個可能適合居住生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們 , 我們太陽系中其他地方的生命發現 , 不論是在土衛二上或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能展示一下 , 基因已經發生了不止一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立的 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 根據推論 , 它已經發生了非常驚人的數量 , 遍及整個宇宙的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是我們所知的唯一行星仍然充滿了生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 它是我們所知的唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們之中有人在1960年代被警告 , 並且我們原諒你 , 如果你沒有 , 好你會記得1968年阿波羅八號太空人拍的這張有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球從太空中被影像出來 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有著巨大的影響 , 我們對我們自己星球的保護有責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼號拍攝了相當於先前的照片 , 一張前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全日蝕 , 從土星的另一端看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張無法想像的美麗圖片中 , 你看到太陽的主要環狀物 , 你看到太陽的折射影像 , 你看到這個環形 , 事實上 , 藉由土衛二的排放而產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 彷彿那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以發現 , 在這個美麗的圖像中 , 看見我們自己的星球 , 在土星光環的臂彎中搖擺 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有件事深深感動 , 看我們自己從遠處看 , 並捕捉到我們在其他世界的天空中的小藍光星球的視覺 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	我們從中得到的這個觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個探索之旅中得到的最好的獎勵 , 是在半個世紀前開始的 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	在2005年 , 只有15%的世界被繪製出來 。 這在災難發生後緩慢了援助的遞送 , 並且隱藏了無用的土地和未知的道路的經濟潛力 。 在這個簡短的演講中 , 谷歌的katragadademos地圖是全球各地的人所使用的組織地圖工具 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故的卡特瓦加達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體系 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 居克羅尼納基斯毀滅了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人受到嚴重的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想趕人和供應該地區
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法幫助到居魯士的受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們觀察洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信在2005年 , 只有15%的世界被繪製成可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國排行榜上 , 大部份的民意臉龐大的問題是:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但協助即將來臨 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40位志願者用一種新的軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路、3000間醫院、物流及解放點 。
and it took them four days .	並且花了他們四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? 谷歌地圖製造商
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	google地圖製造者是一種科技 , 賦予我們每個人去繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地的企業 , 視頻商店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎得主赫南多•索托意識到 , 大部分開發中國家的經濟fff的關鍵在於要剝奪大量的未謀面的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 僅在印度就有一兆美元的房地產仍然沒有被開發出來 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光在去年 , 170個國家就有數以百萬計的使用者繪製了數以百萬計的資訊 , 創造出一張細節的地圖 , 從來沒有想過 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	到處都是熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看一些由使用者所創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 正如我們所說的 , 人們在這些170個國家中繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	更靠近家鄉 , 查盧亞 , 班加羅爾的n.g.道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、手勢辨識 , 以及機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市裡 , 一個使用者 , 一次編輯一次 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是一個邀請到我們未開發的地球上70%的
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 布德魯斯的巴勒斯坦村落成立了十個月的非暴力抗爭 , 阻止了一座圍繞著他們的橄欖岩的障礙 。 你們聽說過嗎 ? 不這麼想 。 巴西製片家朱利亞•巴切納問為什麼我們只關注以色列斯坦衝突的暴力行為 , 而非暴力領袖有一天可能帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:注意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的方式來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我和我在歐洲和美國的作品一起旅行時 , 一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	我在聽到這個問題時所面臨的挑戰 , 通常我剛從中東返回 , 在那裡 , 我花了數十個巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和定居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖要鑄造一個大規模的國家非暴力運動 , 來終結這個職業 , 並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分歧在地面上發生的事情和國外的感知之間的差別是目前為止沒有巴勒斯坦和平抵抗運動已經成功的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我在這裡要談的是注意力的力量 , 你注意力的力量 , 以及西岸、加薩和其他地方非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 但我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大多缺失了要成長的非暴力行為 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經存在的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用帶大家到布德魯斯村來說明這個點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣布它會建立一個隔離障礙 , 其中一部分的障礙會建在村子上 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被包圍 , 所以他們會失去自由接觸西岸的其他地方 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過鼓舞當地的領導 , 他們發起了和平抵抗運動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們對於在地面上實際看起來是什麼樣子的感覺 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知牆壁會分離出以色列的巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯這裡 , 我們了解到牆壁會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:柵欄有 , 事實上 , 創造出恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你受邀參加一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入了 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列行動主義者:沒有什麼比非暴力反對更嚇人的軍隊 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有一個人能這麼做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫派對成員:我們必須要把傳統思維的思維空出來 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯派對成員:我們完全和諧 , 我們想要把它散播到所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	聊:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	fatah , 哈馬斯和流行的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	消息主管:柵欄上的凝塊會持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去散佈群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活著的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	像是faujah , 到處射殺
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列行動主義者:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但身邊還有一些人甚至不是牛仔褲 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	普魯斯特:這是一場和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	聊:我們辦得到 ! 我們辦得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	juliabacha:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很訝異國際媒體並沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功的事實
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民們 , 在十個月的和平抵抗之後 , 說服以色列政府把障礙的路線從他們的土地和綠線上移開 , 也就是在以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的國際認可界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抗藥性 , 自從散播到西岸的村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦鄰居 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而 , 媒體仍然沉默在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會帶來深刻的後果 , 對於非暴力可以成長的可能性 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存的可能性 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力的抗藥性和非暴力抗藥性共有一件非常重要的事 ; 它們都是一種劇院尋求觀眾的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一經常得到頭版的報導 , 吸引了巴勒斯坦議題的國際關注 , 對於非暴力領導者來說 , 要對他們民間不服從的社群來說是可行的選擇 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能會跟房間裡的父母一樣不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子拋出越來越大聲的反抗方式 , 是讓他第一次關注他 , 丟出一個符號 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	抗拒會成為兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為這個孩子已經學到他可以從中得到家長的關注 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以藉由給予孩子的注意力來激勵或不激勵行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以被影響 , 取決於國際社群選擇關注它的注意力所在 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東地區的衝突 , 並帶來和平的核心 , 就是我們把非暴力行為轉化為一種功能性行為 , 做法是對現今地面上的非暴力領導者提供更多注意力 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在將我的影片帶到西岸的村落 , 加薩和東耶路撒冷的村落 , 我看到即使有一部紀錄片也能影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉耶的村落裡 , 位於非常接近耶路撒冷的村落裡 , 這個社區正面臨著與布德魯斯非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去很多土地 , 沒有取得自由 , 不論是西岸還是耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力 , 但自從沒人注意到之後 , 就已經漸漸消失 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個篩檢
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉辦了最好的示威活動 , 去約會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德魯斯在一部電影中記錄下來的布德魯斯的故事 , 感覺到確實有人遵守他們所做的事 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列的一邊 , 有一種新的和平運動叫做 「 固態暴動 」 , 意思是希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者一直在使用布德魯斯作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告 , 以色列人從來沒有活躍過 , 在看電影時 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉耶和固態運動的例子 , 顯示 , 即使是一部小預算獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 轉變為非暴力行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週的非暴力示威 , 發生在村落裡 , 像畢爾、尼德林、華拉雅 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 像席克•賈拉和史爾瓦 , 非暴力領袖在工作中會變得更明顯、重視、有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 彷彿它們從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是我看到了第一手如果我們做到了 , 他們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響力會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力終於可以解開情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導者已經證明了非暴力在像布德魯斯這樣的地方可行 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	來給他們注意力 , 讓他們可以證明它到處都行得通 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙.辛克有個簡單但強大的模型 , 為鼓舞人心的領導 , 一切都始於金圈 , 問題是 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁.路德.金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	野牛、商業、企業家、領導階層、銷售、販賣、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	賽蒙.辛克:偉大領袖如何啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	如何解釋當事情不如我們假設時
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠達成似乎會否定所有假設的事物 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比全部的競爭都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能、相同的機構、同樣的顧問、同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那為什麼他們似乎有不一樣的東西呢 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一在預防美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是當天唯一的偉大演員 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控、有權力的男人飛行 , 當時肯定有其他團隊更好資格、更好的資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	而且他們沒有達到有權力的人飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我做了一個發現
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對我如何看待世界運作的看法 , 它甚至深深地改變了我在裡面運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果是 , 有一個模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果是 , 世界上所有偉大且鼓舞人心的領導者和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁路德金或萊特兄弟 , 他們都認為、行動 , 並以同樣的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是把它編碼出來 , 可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為金色圓圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 為什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領袖能夠啟發其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快的定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們做了什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是怎麼做的 , 不論你稱之為你的區別價值主張、你的屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但極少數的人或組織都知道他們為什麼會做他們的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	藉由 「 為什麼 」 不代表 「 為了賺錢 」
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	到了 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織會存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼早上要下床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們的思考方式、行動方式、溝通的方式 , 都來自外在的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚的東西走到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵人心的領導者和激勵人心的組織 , 不論它們的大小 , 不論它們的產業都在思考 , 行動 , 並從內部向外傳遞 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦是因為它們很容易理解 , 大家都懂了 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和其他人一樣 , 從他們身上得到的行銷訊息可能聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 用起來很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一個嗎 ? " 梅 "
and that's how most of us communicate .	這也是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷就是這樣做 , 大部分的銷售量就是這樣 , 大多數人在人際交流的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的事 , 我們說我們是如何不同或如何變得更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師 , 有最大的客戶 , 我們總是為跟我們做生意的客戶表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它會得到很棒的氣體里程數 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果電腦是這樣傳達的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 簡單地使用和友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧做出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同對吧 ? 你準備從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是把資訊的順序反過來 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明了人們不會買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一個人都完全不舒服從蘋果電腦購買電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也完全舒服的購買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能區分出他們和任何競爭者的結構 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格做出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway和平面螢幕電視一起出櫃 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格做平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在做平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾出版了mp3播放器和pdas , 他們製作了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的設計 , 沒有人買了一台 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在談到這件事 , 我們甚至無法想像從迪爾去買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從電腦公司買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和所有需要你擁有的東西的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人們做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我告訴你們的 , 沒有一個是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都在生物學的網絡裡著手 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的十字架 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是人腦 , 其實是被分為三個主要元件 , 與黃金圈完美相關聯 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 對應的是 「 什麼 」 的層級 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性和分析思考和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部份組成了我們的邊緣腦 , 我們的邊緣腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外在溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部向外溝通時 , 我們會直接和控制行為的腦部溝通 , 接著 , 我們會讓人們用我們說、做的事來合理化 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策來自的地方 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給某人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說了些什麼 , 但這感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用那個動詞 , 不是 「 感覺 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦部不會控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好能站出來的是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或有時你會說你帶著你的心 , 或你帶著你的靈魂領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭把它分解給你 , 那些不是身體的部位在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的腦中 , 大腦控制決策而非語言的那部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你會做的事 , 人們會回應為什麼你會做你的事 , 那你要如何讓別人投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠且想要成為你做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你擁有的東西的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要雇用需要工作的人 , 而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這樣說 , 如果你雇用人 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢而工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的 , 他們會為你工作 , 帶著血汗和淚水流 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有一個比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀初期 , 追求有權的人飛行就像是當天的點 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley擁有的 , 我們假設是成功的配方 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你也問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你同樣的三樣東西的突變:不合時宜、錯人、壞市場狀況 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是相同的三樣東西 , 所以我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley透過戰爭部門得到五萬美金來找出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦了座位 , 在史密森尼亞工作 , 非常精通 ; 他知道當時所有的大頭腦 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的心智錢可以找到 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報到處跟著他 , 每個人都為langley紮根 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們怎麼從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	在俄亥俄州的幾百英里外 , 俄亥俄州的奧維爾和威爾•萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的配方 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們拿著腳踏車店的夢想來支付 , 而不是萊特兄弟團隊裡的單人有大學教育 , 甚至不是奧維爾或威爾堡 ; 而紐約時報也隨處可見 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾堡被一個原因所驅使 , 由一個目的 , 一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能弄清楚這台飛行機器 , 就會改變世界的過程 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley有所不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變富有 , 想成為名人
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果時
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人時
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想和他們一起工作的人用血汗和淚水
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只為了支付支付而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說故事 , 每當萊特兄弟出門時 , 他們就得拿五組零件 , 因為那是他們在去供應商前撞到的次數 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟搭飛機 , 甚至沒有人去那裡體驗 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明langley受到了錯誤的動機:萊特兄弟搭飛機的那天 , 他戒掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那真是個了不起的發現 , 各位 , 我會改進你們的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有成名 , 所以他放棄 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的那些人是很重要的 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂的 「 創新法則 」 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5%是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數、遲到的大多數和護士 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸感電話的唯一理由 , 是因為你再也買不到轉帳電話 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個規模的各個地方 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大規模市場成功或大規模市場接受一個想法 , 你無法擁有它 , 直到你達成了15%到18%的市場滲透 , 然後系統就會提高 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新事業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你: 「 喔 , 大約是10% 。 」 驕傲地說 ,
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以跳過超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種直覺 , 「 喔 , 他們只是得到了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們一起做生意之前 , 如何找到那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 就是這個 , 這個你必須關閉的小缺口 , 正如傑佛瑞•摩爾所說的 , 「 跨越隔閡 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多數的人會先嘗試 , 直到別人先嘗試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很舒服地做這些決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒服地做出那些直覺性的決定 , 由他們對世界的看法所驅使 , 而不只是產品是可以取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站了六個小時去買iphone , 當他們剛出櫃時 , 可以在下週走進商店買單 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了4萬美金在平面電視上當他們初次出櫃時 , 儘管這項技術是次級的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順道一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己也這麼做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想成為首要
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不會買你做什麼 ; 他們會買你為什麼做 , 你做的只是證明你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	那個人在前六小時買了iphone的原因 , 站在線上六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們希望每個人如何看待他們:他們是第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	所以 , 讓我舉一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及一個有名的成功 , 是關於創新法則的擴散法則 。
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 著名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	一個商業的例子
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說 , 第二年前 , 成功的配方是金錢和對的人和對的市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八九年前tivo出來的時代到現在的日子 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下是沒有爭議的 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受惠 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是把東西放在垃圾時間華納dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是商業失敗的
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是30或40美元 , 然後跌倒 , 從來沒有在10歲以上交易過 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它甚至在六上方交易 , 只不過有幾個小漏洞 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個可以暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過商業廣告 , 反轉現場電視 , 並記住你看過的習慣 , 甚至不用你問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 , 我們不喜歡
you're scaring us . "	你嚇壞了我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你人生的各個面向的人 , 男孩 , 我們是否有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視 , 跳過商業廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 而你所做的事就是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我舉一個成功的例子來說明創新法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有25萬人在華盛頓的商場上出現 , 聽見金恩博士說話 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們發出沒有邀請函 , 當時沒有網站來查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士並不是美國唯一一個偉大的演員 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一受苦於預防美國的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很不好 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處去告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的人們 , 把他的成因弄成了他們自己 , 告訴別人 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	而其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓這個詞能傳遞給更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	有25萬人在右天出席 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們對美國的信念 , 讓他們在一輛公車上旅行八個小時 , 站在華盛頓的陽光下 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人對白:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信 , 在這個世界上有兩種法律:那些由更高權威者所制訂的法律 , 和那些由人類製造的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由男人制定的法律都和更高權威制定的法律一致 , 我們才會活在一個公正的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	公民權利運動實在是太完美了 , 來協助他帶來人生的原因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨了 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順道一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 的演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計劃 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽聽現在的政治人物 , 帶著他們全面的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者和有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者握有權力或權威的立場 , 但那些領導人啟發我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論他們是個人或組織 , 我們都會跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人有能力去激勵他們周圍的人 , 或找尋那些激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你把車子停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是往正確的方向移動的 ? 神經科學家尼爾•布里奇斯研究了我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結到記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburgeges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 ?
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大型停車場時 , 我們怎麼記得我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬面臨的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	並試著去了解他大腦中發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以我們會從海馬體開始 , 以黃色表示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那裡受損 , 像在阿茲海默症 , 你記不得東西包括你把車停在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	以拉丁文命名為 「 海馬 」 , 它會重新組合 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以 , 人類的大腦中大約有一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	而神經元彼此間的溝通 , 藉由傳送小脈衝或電流 , 通過互相連結來傳遞訊息 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成的 , 非常緊密的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 做法是從老鼠身上的個別神經元或老鼠身上記錄下來 , 同時覓食或探索一個尋找食物的環境 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以我們會想像我們從這隻老鼠的海馬體中的一個神經元記錄下來 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它激發電力時 , 會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們看到這個神經元知道每當老鼠在它的環境中進入某個特定的位置時
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送一點電流刺激 , 它會傳送到大腦的其他部分 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以把神經元的發育率呈現為動物的位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物在其環境中的不同部分 , 不同的神經元會發射出來 , 就像在這個方形的盒子裡所顯示的 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們一起組成了大腦的地圖 , 不斷告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以 , 癲癇患者有時需要他們腦部監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	其中一些病人玩電玩遊戲 , 他們開車繞過一個小鎮 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	而在牠們的嬉皮身上的細胞會發動 , 變得活躍 , 每當牠們開車經過一個特定的城鎮時 , 就會發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 細胞如何知道老鼠或人在它的環境中在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	嗯 , 這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界限特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	頂端的那個會喜歡在他們老鼠的盒子牆壁之間打火 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你把箱子擴大時 , 激發的位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面那一顆很喜歡開火 , 每當有一面牆靠近南方時 ,
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一道牆放進箱子裡 , 細胞在兩個地方都會發射到南邊 , 當動物在箱子裡探索時 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這預測了 , 感應你周圍的界線和方向 , 延伸出去的建築物等等 , 對海馬體來說 , 尤其重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體輸入到海馬體時 , 細胞會在海馬體中找到哪些專案 , 它的確會對偵測範圍的距離或邊緣有著特定的距離 , 以及從老鼠或老鼠四處探索的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每當動物靠近牆壁時 , 或向東邊邊界線時 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣或圓形牆壁 , 甚至是圓形盒的邊緣 , 動物都跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發射 , 當南邊有界線時 , 不論是桌邊的一滴 , 一面牆壁 , 甚至兩張桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 這是我們認為 , 放置細胞來決定動物四處探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體的位置 , 比如這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車子在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放到他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們用細胞所做的 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉個例子 , 如果旗幟處在一個小方形的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們 , 它在哪裡 , 但你讓環境更大 , 他們認為旗幟已經被伸展出完全一樣的位置細胞發射 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你記得旗幟在哪裡 , 藉由在那個位置的位置細胞在你所在位置的位置 , 通過移動 , 你最好的配合你位置細胞的發射模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想記得的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過動作的位置 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們把一些外來的路徑拿走 , 或許我們會停下來 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 可以整合到這條路上 , 大約是要回去的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	安置細胞也會從一種叫做網格細胞的細胞中得到這種路徑的整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞又被發現了 , 在海馬體的輸入點上 , 它們有點像放置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠在周圍探索時 , 每個個別細胞會在一系列的不同位置發射 , 在環境中 , 形成一個非常驚人的三角形網格 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從這裡的幾個網格細胞記錄下來 , 每種顏色都有像網格般的激發模式 , 每個細胞的網格激發模式會稍微轉移到其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	這張網格上的紅色部分和綠色的部分 , 上面是藍色的 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 一起 , 就好像老鼠可以放一個虛擬的網格 , 橫跨它的環境 , 有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線 , 但使用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電力活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的所在位置 , 讓它可以用它自己的動作來知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有像網格一樣的激發模式都有相同的對稱軸 , 相同的網格 , 以橘色表示 , 所有格子的網格活動都應該根據我們沿著這六個方向跑 , 或沿著其中一個六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振影像掃描儀中 , 讓他們做個小電玩遊戲 , 就像我給你看的那個 , 尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你的確在人類的眼皮層看到了它 , 這和你在老鼠身上看到網格細胞的相同部分 。
so back to homer .	所以回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他大概還記得他的車在哪裡 , 用距離和方向把建築和界線延伸到他所在的位置 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被邊界偵測細胞的激發所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也還記得他從車子公園拿出來的路 , 這條路會在網格細胞的激發中呈現 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發火 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以重返停車位的位置 , 通過移動 , 找到最好的位置細胞在他大腦中產生的發育模式 , 用他停車的儲存模式 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個視覺暗示的地點 , 像是他的車是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許已經被鎮定了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去找它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找像網格般激盪的模式 , 我們會在一系列的位置看到 , 當我們做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 總是很活躍的 , 比如記住你上次去參加婚禮 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是 , 代表我們周遭空間的神經機制 , 也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們就能重現空間的場景 , 至少 , 在我們想要想像的時候 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生了這種狀況 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 透過這些密集的相互連結 , 然後重新啟動邊緣細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種我還沒提到的細胞 , 頭部朝向細胞 , 它們會根據你所面臨的方向來發射 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以從你想要的視覺圖像來定義觀看方向 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個婚禮時發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以 , 這只是一個新時代的一個例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 比如你如何記得、想像 , 甚至是以數十億個神經元組成大腦的動作來思考 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全是由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾合作所驅動的 。 那不只是開放原始碼粉絲的遙遠希望 , 是詹姆士史塔里地斯的遠景 , 北約的最高指揮官 , 他們從近代的軍事歷史中分享生動的時刻 , 來解釋為什麼未來的安全性應該是用橋樑來建造而非牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史崔迪斯:nato的最高指揮官如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我現在要談的是開放原始碼的安全性 , 因為我們必須在21世紀更好的安全性 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 讓我們回顧一下二十世紀 , 有點像是對我們來說安全的風格 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的戰場就在比利時的北方北部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年的verdun , 超過300天的時期 , 有70萬人被殺 , 所以每天大約2000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它向前推進20世紀的安全性轉移到第二次世界大戰中 , 你會看到史達林升級的戰役 , 300天 , 2百萬人被殺 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一場世界大戰的第一場戰役 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬吉諾線 , 然後進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
